الأشياء
أي ظهر
درك الحواس يعني العقل نور يتضح به طريق ابتدائه من موضع ينتهي إليه درك الحواس؛ لأن الإنسان إذا بصر بناء وانتهى إليه حسن البصر يدرك بعقله أن له بانياً ذا حياة وقدرة وعلم، فهذا طريق ابتداؤه من حيث انتهى إليه درك الحواس وهو البناء، وهذا الطريق اتضح بسبب العقل وهو : أي العقل في الملك الباطن الملكوت أي الملك والتاء زائدة للمبالغة كالجبروت والرغبوت :بزغت أي طلعت الشمس والجملة الشرطية تعليل لقوله: "وهو كالشمس بشهابها : أي بنورها من غير أن توجب الشمس رؤية تلك الأشياء، فكذا القلب يدرك ما هو غائب عن الحواس بنور العقل من غير أن يكون العقل موجباً لذلك. ف: اعلم أن في هذه العبارة إشارة إلى ردّ المعتزلة المخالفين لنا في مسألة النظر، وإني سأتلو عليك تفصيل المذاهب فيها، وأبين ما هو الحق فيها، فاعلم - أرشدك الله تعالى - أن عند الأشعري إفادة النظر العلم بالعادة لا دخل للنظر في الإفادة أصلاً ليس علة تامة ولا ناقصة، بل العلم يدور معه دوران أمر مع آخر، لا علاقة بينهما في الأكثر أو الدائم كوجود الإنسان مع الحمار، فلو كان الإنسان موجوداً بلا وجود حمار أو بالعكس فلا مضائقة؛ إذ لا مؤثر عنده إلا الله تعالى بمعنى أنه المستقل، لكنه فاعل مختار، فصدور المعلول عنه بلا وجوب منه كما ذهب إليه الفلاسفة؛ لأن الوجوب ينافي الاختيار، ولا وجوب عليه كما ذهب إليه المعتزلة والشيعة من وجوب اللطف عليه تعالى وأما عند المعتزلة فالإفادة بالتوليد، وهو عبارة عن إيجاد فعل بتوسط فعل آخر کحركة المفتاح بحركة اليد، وكالألم بعد الضرب، فإذا باشر النظر يحدث بعده العلم، كما إذا ضرب رجل رجلا فبمباشرة الضرب يحصل الألم بعده، وأما عند الحكماء فبطريق الإعداد، فإن النظر يعد الذهن إعدادا تاما، فيفيض عليه العلم من المبدأ الفياض وجوباً منه هذا تفصيل المذاهب والحق أن العلم واجب عقيب النظر وإن لم يكن واجبا منه تعالى غير متولد من النظر كما ذهب إليه المعتزلة.
أما الوجوب فلأن كل من علم أن العالم متغيّر وكل متغير حادث فمع حضور هذين العلمين في الذهن يستحيل أن لا يعلم أنه حادث، والعلم بهذا الامتناع ضروري، وأما إبطال التوليد فلأن العلم ممكن في نفسه وإن كان بعد النظر، وكل ممكن مقدور له تعالى، فيكون هو أيضا مقدورا الله تعالى، فيمتنع وقوعه بغير قدرته، وهذا هو مختار الإمام الرازي، وإليه ذهب القاضي أبو بكر الباقلاني وإمام الحرمين و به ارتضى صاحب المسلم، =
When he finished explaining the schools regarding the consideration of intellect and its non-consideration, he began its definition, saying: It is a light, etc. In the human body, it is said its place is the brain according to philosophers, and the heart according to usul scholars. The meaning of light is manifestation; it is manifest and manifests like the light of the sun, for by it one sees sensibles. Similarly, intellect is a light by which the realities and inner aspects of things are perceived. Rather, intellect is more worthy of the name 'light' because by it one is guided to intelligibles, unlike sunlight, which is a means to perceive sensibles.

Chapter of Qiyas
Differences of people regarding intellect
The perception of the senses: so the sought object appears to the heart, and the heart perceives it by its contemplation with the help of Allah.
That is, it appears not by its necessitation. It is like the sun in the visible kingdom; when it rises and its rays appear and the path becomes clear, the eye perceives by its light.
That is, by the light of the sun.
.
Things
That is, appeared.
Perception of the senses means that intellect is a light by which the path is clarified, its beginning from where the perception of the senses ends. Because when a person sees a building and his eyesight reaches it, he perceives by his intellect that it has a builder with life, power, and knowledge. So this is a path whose beginning is where the perception of the senses ended, i.e., the building, and this path is clarified by intellect. And it is: the intellect in the inner kingdom, i.e., kingdom, with the 'ta' for exaggeration like jabarut and raghbut. 'Bazaghat' means the sun rose, and the conditional sentence is the explanation of his statement: 'It is like the sun with its light' i.e., by its light without the sun necessitating the seeing of those things. So too the heart perceives what is absent from the senses by the light of intellect without intellect necessitating that.
So know that in this expression there is a reference to refuting the Mu'tazila who opposed us on the question of nazar (speculative reasoning). I will present to you the details of the schools on it and clarify what is the truth. Know, may Allah guide you, that according to al-Ash'ari, nazar produces knowledge by habit; nazar has no role in producing it at all—neither as a complete nor an incomplete cause. Rather, knowledge co-occurs with it like one thing with another, with no relationship between them most of the time or permanently, like the existence of a human with a donkey. So if a human exists without a donkey, or vice versa, there is no problem. For according to him, there is no effect except Allah, meaning He is independent, but He is a free agent. So the effect proceeds from Him without necessity from Him, as the philosophers held, because necessity negates choice. And there is no necessity upon Him as the Mu'tazila and Shi'a held regarding the necessity of grace upon Him. According to the Mu'tazila, the production is by generation (tawlid), which is the creation of an act through another act, like the movement of a key by the movement of a hand, and like pain after hitting. So when one engages in nazar, knowledge occurs after it, as when a man hits another, by the act of hitting, pain occurs after it. According to the philosophers, it is by way of preparation (i'dad): nazar prepares the mind completely, then knowledge overflows upon it from the overflowing principle necessarily from it. This is the detail of the schools. The truth is that knowledge is necessary after nazar, although it is not necessary from Him, nor generated from nazar as the Mu'tazila held.
As for its necessity: because anyone who knows that the world is changing and everything changing is temporal, with these two pieces of knowledge present in the mind, it is impossible not to know that it is temporal. And knowledge of this impossibility is necessary. As for invalidating generation: because knowledge is possible in itself even if it is after nazar, and everything possible is within His power. So it is also within the power of Allah, and it is impossible for it to occur without His power. This is the chosen view of Imam al-Razi, and Abu Bakr al-Baqillani and Imam al-Haramayn went to it, and the author (sahib al-Muslim) approved it.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on Qiyas by first elaborating the definition of intellect through an analogy with sunlight, emphasizing that intellect manifests realities without causing them. The author then explicitly addresses the dispute on nazar (speculative reasoning) and its role in producing knowledge. He outlines three positions: (1) Ash'ari: knowledge co-occurs with nazar by habit, with no causal relationship; (2) Mu'tazila: nazar generates knowledge like a physical cause; (3) Philosophers: nazar prepares the mind for knowledge to overflow. The Hanafi position, as chosen by leading scholars like al-Razi, is that knowledge is necessarily subsequent to nazar, but this necessity is not due to generation or divine compulsion—rather it is a logical necessity given the premises, and the knowledge itself is created by Allah. The author provides a rational proof: if one knows the premises, it is impossible not to know the conclusion (knowledge is necessary), but the knowledge itself is a possible thing, so it must be from Allah's power, not generated by the act of nazar.

Key Terms
النظر (al-naẓar): Speculative reasoning aimed at acquiring knowledge; it is the act of examining evidence (dalil) to reach a conclusion.
التوليد (al-tawlīd): The Mu'tazili concept that one act generates another necessarily, like movement generating key movement or hitting generating pain.
الإعداد (al-iʿdād): Preparation: the philosopher's view that nazar prepares the mind to receive knowledge from the active intellect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position described, why does knowledge necessarily follow nazar?
A) Because nazar generates knowledge like a cause.
B) Because it is logically impossible to know the premises and not know the conclusion.
C) Because Allah compels the knowledge without the need for nazar.
D) Because the mind is prepared by nazar to overflow knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Speculative reasoning (nazar) necessarily leads to knowledge, but that knowledge is a creation of Allah, not a human product.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
8 min
How Does Reason Produce Knowledge? The Four Views
Examines four views on how reasoning leads to knowledge of God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four major positions on how reason produces knowledge (or not) and evaluate the Hanafi/Imam al-Razi synthesis.

Core Idea
Reason does not generate knowledge; it is a tool through which God creates knowledge after reflection.

This passage presents a foundational usul dispute: does the intellect alone necessitate knowledge of God, or is divine intervention required? The author compares the Ash'ari, Mu'tazili, Philosopher, and Hanafi positions, then defends the view that knowledge is necessary after reasoning but is not generated by it. Understanding this dispute is crucial for determining who is legally obligated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four schools
List the four positions: Ash'ari (habit), Mu'tazila (generation/tawlid), Philosophers (preparation/i'dad), and the 'truth' (knowledge necessary after reasoning, but from God).
The 'truth' is attributed to Imam al-Razi and others.
2
Analyze each school's claim
For each school, state the causal mechanism (or lack thereof) between reasoning and knowledge.
Ash'ari: no causality, only correlation. Mu'tazila: direct generation. Philosophers: preparation leading to necessary emanation. Hanafi: knowledge is created by God after reasoning.
3
Examine the Hanafi refutation of tawlid
The author argues that if knowledge is possible and within God's power, it cannot occur without His will. This refutes the Mu'tazili idea that reasoning necessitates knowledge.
The argument uses the principle that every possible (mumkin) is under God's power.
4
Evaluate the thamarah (practical consequence)
Consider how each school's stance affects the obligation of a person who has not received revelation.
This connects to the next lesson on taklif.

باب القياس
اختلاف الناس في العقل
درك الحواس، فيبدو المطلوب للقلب فيدركه القلب بتأمله بتوفيق الله تعالى أي يظهر لا بإيجابه وهو كالشمس في الملكوت الظاهرة إذا بزغت وبدا شعاعها ووضح الطريق كانت العين مدركة بشهابها، بسبب ضوء الشمس الأشياء أي ظهر درك الحواس يعني العقل نور يتضح به طريق ابتدائه من موضع ينتهي إليه درك الحواس؛ لأن الإنسان إذا بصر بناء وانتهى إليه حسن البصر يدرك بعقله أن له بانياً ذا حياة وقدرة وعلم، فهذا طريق ابتداؤه من حيث انتهى إليه درك الحواس وهو البناء، وهذا الطريق اتضح بسبب العقل وهو : أي العقل في الملك الباطن الملكوت أي الملك والتاء زائدة للمبالغة كالجبروت والرغبوت :بزغت أي طلعت الشمس والجملة الشرطية تعليل لقوله: "وهو كالشمس بشهابها : أي بنورها من غير أن توجب الشمس رؤية تلك الأشياء، فكذا القلب يدرك ما هو غائب عن الحواس بنور العقل من غير أن يكون العقل موجباً لذلك. ف: اعلم أن في هذه العبارة إشارة إلى ردّ المعتزلة المخالفين لنا في مسألة النظر، وإني سأتلو عليك تفصيل المذاهب فيها، وأبين ما هو الحق فيها، فاعلم - أرشدك الله تعالى - أن عند الأشعري إفادة النظر العلم بالعادة لا دخل للنظر في الإفادة أصلاً ليس علة تامة ولا ناقصة، بل العلم يدور معه دوران أمر مع آخر، لا علاقة بينهما في الأكثر أو الدائم كوجود الإنسان مع الحمار، فلو كان الإنسان موجوداً بلا وجود حمار أو بالعكس فلا مضائقة؛ إذ لا مؤثر عنده إلا الله تعالى بمعنى أنه المستقل، لكنه فاعل مختار، فصدور المعلول عنه بلا وجوب منه كما ذهب إليه الفلاسفة؛ لأن الوجوب ينافي الاختيار، ولا وجوب عليه كما ذهب إليه المعتزلة والشيعة من وجوب اللطف عليه تعالى وأما عند المعتزلة فالإفادة بالتوليد، وهو عبارة عن إيجاد فعل بتوسط فعل آخر کحركة المفتاح بحركة اليد، وكالألم بعد الضرب، فإذا باشر النظر يحدث بعده العلم، كما إذا ضرب رجل رجلا فبمباشرة الضرب يحصل الألم بعده، وأما عند الحكماء فبطريق الإعداد، فإن النظر يعد الذهن إعدادا تاما، فيفيض عليه العلم من المبدأ الفياض وجوباً منه هذا تفصيل المذاهب والحق أن العلم واجب عقيب النظر وإن لم يكن واجبا منه تعالى غير متولد من النظر كما ذهب إليه المعتزلة.
أما الوجوب فلأن كل من علم أن العالم متغيّر وكل متغير حادث فمع حضور هذين العلمين في الذهن يستحيل أن لا يعلم أنه حادث، والعلم بهذا الامتناع ضروري، وأما إبطال التوليد فلأن العلم ممكن في نفسه وإن كان بعد النظر، وكل ممكن مقدور له تعالى، فيكون هو أيضا مقدورا الله تعالى، فيمتنع وقوعه بغير قدرته، وهذا هو مختار الإمام الرازي، وإليه ذهب القاضي أبو بكر الباقلاني وإمام الحرمين و به ارتضى صاحب المسلم،
وما بالعقل كفاية. ولهذا قلنا: إن الصبي غير مكلف بالإيمان، حتى إذا عقلت المراهقة وهي تحت مسلم بين أبوين مسلمين ولم تصف الإسلام لم تجعل مرتدة ولم تبن من زوجها ولو بلغت كذلك لبانت من زوجها وكذا نقول في الذي في العاقل البالغ لم تبلغه الدعوة: إنه غير مكلف بمجرد العقل، وإنه إذا لم يصف إيمانا ولا كفرا بالإيمان و لم يعتقد على شيء كان معذوراً
وقال شارحه مولانا نظام الدين له: فالأصلح الوجوب، وكون النظر علة قريبة والفياض هو الله تعالى، ولذلك يحكم العقل بالوجوب، ولم أجد هذا المعنى مخالفاً للنصوص الإلهية والنبوية. فتدبر في هذا المقام، فإنه من مزال الأقدام. كفاية: يعني وإن كان العقل آلة للإدراك ولكنه ليس بكاف في حصول المعرفة بغير توفيق الله تعالى. هذا ما قال بعض الشراح، والأولى أن يقال: إن العقل وإن كان يعرف قبح الأفعال وحسنها ولكنه ليس بمستبد في ذلك أي ليس بمستقل، حتى يتحقق الأحكام بمجرد العقل من غير ورود الشرع، كما هو مذهب المعتزلة. غير مكلف بالإيمان: أي الإيمان ليس بواجب عليه؛ لأن الوجوب وكذا سائر الأحكام بالخطاب لا بمجرد العقل، وهو غير مكلف لقوله عليه السلام: "رفع القلم عن ثلاث: عن النائم حتى يستيقظ، وعن الصبي حتى يبلغ، وعن المعتوه حتى يعقل". رواه الترمذي رقم: ١٤٢٣ وأبو داود والدارمي عن عائشة وابن ماجة عنها وأحمد، وصححه الحاكم، ولكنه لو آمن يصح إيمانه لوجود العقل، وعند الأشعرية إيمانه غير صحيح؛ إذ العقل لا يعبأ به عندهم، والاعتبار بالشرع، وفي حقه الشرع ليس موجود؛ لأنه غير مكلف، وعند المعتزلة لما كان العقل كافياً يجب عليه الإيمان وإن لم يرد به الشرع. المراهقة: هي المرأة التي قاربت البلوغ. وهي تحت مسلم إلخ بيان لإسلامها الحكمي بوجه لبانت من زوجها : يعني إذا كانت المرأة عاقلة ولكن لم تبلغ وهي تحت عبد مسلم، فاستوصف منها الإسلام ولم تقدر على البيان لا يحكم بردتها؛ لأن الردة خروج عن الإسلام وهي لم تكن مسلمة قبل لعدم قدرتها على وصف الإسلام، فلايحكم بردتها ولكن هي غير مكلفة بالإسلام بسبب عدم البلوغ؛ إذ العقل وإن كان موجوداً فيها لكنه غير كاف فإذا لم يجب عليها الإسلام لاتبين عن زوجها. نعم لو بلغت ووجب عليها الإسلام وهي بعد البلوغ أيضاً لاتقدر على وصف الإسلام لبانت من زوجها البتة وكذا أي كما قلنا في الصبي العاقل: إنه غير مكلف بالإيمان لعدم كفاية عقله تغيّر ورود الشرع في حقه بسبب عدم بلوغه كذا نقول في: إلخ. الله الدعوة: أي دعوة الرسول أو من قام مقامه بأن يكون على شاهق الجبل ولم يبق بعد البلوغ حتى يعينه بالتجربة ودرك العواقب كان معذوراً : هذا إذا مات بعد البلوغ من ساعته، فإذا لم تبلغه الدعوة ولم يأته مما هو قائم مقام الدعوة وزمان النظر والاستدلال على توحيده سبحانه وتعالى.
•
بوجه أكد.
Chapter of Qiyas. The disagreement of people regarding the intellect. The perception of the senses... the desired thing appears to the heart and the heart perceives it by reflecting upon it with the help of Allah Almighty, i.e., it appears, not by its necessitation. It is like the sun in the visible kingdom; when it rises and its rays appear and the path becomes clear, the eye perceives [objects] by its radiance, due to the light of the sun. The things appear. The perception of the senses means that the intellect is a light by which the path from its starting point to the point where the perception of the senses ends becomes clear. Because when a person sees a building and his sight reaches its end, he perceives with his intellect that it has a builder possessing life, power, and knowledge. This is a path whose starting point is where the perception of the senses ended, i.e., the building, and this path becomes clear due to the intellect. [The commentator says:] 'He' meaning the intellect in the inner kingdom, i.e., the kingdom, and the 'ta' is added for exaggeration like jabarut and raghbut. 'Bazaghat' means the sun rose, and the conditional sentence is an explanation of his statement: 'It is like the sun with its radiance,' i.e., by its light, without the sun necessitating the vision of those things. Similarly, the heart perceives what is absent from the senses by the light of the intellect, without the intellect being the necessitator of that. Know that in this expression there is an indication of refuting the Mu'tazila who oppose us in the matter of reasoning. I will recite to you the details of the schools of thought in it and clarify what is true in it. Know... that according to Ash'ari, reasoning produces knowledge by habit; reasoning has no role in production at all, it is neither a complete nor an incomplete cause. Rather, knowledge goes along with it as one thing goes with another, without any relation between them in most or always, like the existence of a human with a donkey. So if a human exists without a donkey existing or vice versa, there is no problem; because according to him there is no effect except Allah, meaning He alone is independent, and He is a free agent. So the effect proceeds from Him without necessity from Him, as the philosophers held, because necessity contradicts free choice. And there is no obligation upon Him as the Mu'tazila and Shi'a held regarding the obligation of grace upon Him. According to the Mu'tazila, production is by generation (tawlid), which is the creation of an act by means of another act, like the movement of a key by the movement of a hand, and like pain after a blow. So when one engages in reasoning, knowledge arises after it, just as when a man strikes a man, by directly striking, pain occurs after it. According to the philosophers, it is by way of preparation (i'dad); reasoning prepares the mind fully, then knowledge flows upon it from the Emanating Principle necessarily from Him. This is the detail of the schools. The truth is that knowledge is necessary (wajib) after reasoning, although it is not necessary from Him [i.e., His action is not compelled], nor is it generated from reasoning as the Mu'tazila held. As for the necessity, because everyone who knows that the world is changing and everything changing is originated (hadith), when these two pieces of knowledge are present in the mind, it is impossible that he does not know that it is originated, and knowledge of this impossibility is necessary. As for invalidating generation, because knowledge is possible in itself although it comes after reasoning, and everything possible is subject to the power of Allah, so it is also within the power of Allah, and it is impossible for it to occur without His power. This is the choice of Imam al-Razi, and Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani and Imam al-Haramayn agreed, and the author of al-Muslim approved. And by the intellect is not sufficiency. Therefore we said: the child (sabi) is not obligated to have faith (iman), so that if a girl approaching puberty (murahiqa) who is under a Muslim husband between two Muslim parents cannot describe Islam, she is not considered an apostate and does not separate from her husband. But if she reaches puberty similarly, she separates from her husband. Similarly, we say regarding the one who is an adult of sound mind who has not received the call: he is not obligated by mere intellect, and if he does not describe faith nor disbelief by faith and does not believe in anything, he is excused. And his commentator, our master Nizam al-Din, said: the most correct is the necessity, and that reasoning is a proximate cause and the Emanator is Allah, therefore the intellect rules with necessity, and I have not found this meaning contradictory to the divine and prophetic texts. So reflect on this station, for it is a slippery place. 'Sufficiency': means although the intellect is an instrument of perception, it is not sufficient for obtaining knowledge without the help of Allah. This is what some commentators said. The better view is to say: the intellect, although it knows the evil and good of actions, is not independent in that, i.e., not autonomous, so that rulings are realized by mere intellect without the arrival of the Sharia, as is the doctrine of the Mu'tazila. 'Not obligated to faith': i.e., faith is not obligatory upon him; because obligation and all other rulings are by address (khitab), not by mere intellect. And he is not obligated due to his statement: 'The pen is lifted from three: from the sleeper until he wakes, from the child until he reaches puberty, and from the insane until he becomes sane.' Narrated by Tirmidhi no. 1423, Abu Dawud, al-Darimi from Aisha, Ibn Majah from her, and Ahmad, and authenticated by al-Hakim. But if he believes, his faith is valid due to the presence of intellect. According to the Ash'aris, his faith is not valid; because they give no weight to intellect, and the consideration is with the Sharia, and in his case the Sharia is not present because he is not obligated. According to the Mu'tazila, since the intellect is sufficient, faith becomes obligatory upon him even if the Sharia does not come. 'Murahiqa': she is the woman close to puberty. 'She is under a Muslim' etc. is an explanation of her legal Islam in a certain way, 'she separates from her husband' means if the woman is intelligent but has not reached puberty and she is under a Muslim husband, and she is asked to describe Islam and cannot do so, she is not judged to be an apostate; because apostasy is leaving Islam, and she was not Muslim before due to her inability to describe Islam, so she is not judged to be an apostate. But she is not obligated to Islam due to not reaching puberty; for even though intellect is present in her, it is not sufficient. So if Islam is not obligatory upon her, she does not separate from her husband. Indeed, if she reaches puberty and Islam becomes obligatory upon her, and even after puberty she still cannot describe Islam, she definitely separates from her husband. Similarly, as we said regarding the intelligent child: he is not obligated to faith due to the insufficiency of his intellect and the change of the arrival of the Sharia in his case due to his not reaching puberty. Similarly, we say regarding: etc. 'The call': i.e., the call of the Messenger or whoever stands in his place, such as being on a mountain top and there remains no one after puberty to assist him through experience and understanding of consequences. 'He is excused': this is if he dies after puberty immediately. So if the call has not reached him and nothing has come to him that stands in the place of the call and the time of reasoning and inferring the oneness of Allah, the Most High, he is excused. With emphasis.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the epistemological role of the intellect (aql) in acquiring knowledge, particularly knowledge of God, and its legal ramifications for obligation (taklif). The author begins by describing the intellect as a light that enables the heart to perceive what is beyond the senses, similar to how sunlight enables vision. He then contrasts four schools of thought on how knowledge arises from reasoning (nazar): the Ash'aris hold that reasoning produces knowledge only by custom (adah) and God is the sole agent; the Mu'tazila claim that reasoning generates knowledge directly (tawlid); the philosophers assert that reasoning prepares the mind and knowledge flows necessarily from the First Principle; and the truth according to the author (following Imam al-Razi) is that knowledge is necessary (wajib) after reasoning, but it is neither caused by reasoning nor necessitated from God—it is within God's power. The author refutes generation (tawlid) by arguing that knowledge is possible, and every possible is within God's power, so it cannot occur without His power. He then applies this principle to legal obligation: the intellect alone does not impose obligations. A child (sabi) is not obligated to have faith, as evidenced by the hadith that the pen is lifted from three categories. The example of a girl approaching puberty (murahiqa) under a Muslim husband illustrates that she is not considered an apostate if she cannot describe Islam, because she is not yet obligated. If she reaches puberty and still cannot describe it, she becomes an apostate. Similarly, an adult who has not received the call of Islam is not obligated by mere intellect and is excused. The commentator Mulla Nizam al-Din adds that the intellect can rule with necessity but only as a proximate cause, and that this view does not contradict revelation. The correct doctrine is that the intellect is neither autonomous nor sufficient; obligation results from divine address (khitab), not reason alone. This refutes the Mu'tazila who deem intellect sufficient and the Ash'aris who dismiss it entirely.

Key Terms
توليد (tawlid): The doctrine that one act directly generates another as cause and effect, e.g., reasoning generating knowledge.
إعداد (i'dad): The preparative role of reasoning in disposing the mind to receive knowledge, without necessitating it.
عادة (adah): Custom; in Ash'ari usul, the regular occurrence of knowledge after reasoning is by God's custom, not causality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following best describes the Hanafi position (Imam al-Razi's choice) on the relationship between reasoning and knowledge?
A) Reasoning generates knowledge by causal necessity (tawlid).
B) Reasoning prepares the mind for knowledge to flow necessarily from God.
C) Knowledge occurs after reasoning, but it is created by God, not generated or necessitated.
D) Reasoning and knowledge are unrelated; knowledge comes only from revelation.

Key Takeaway
Knowledge is necessary after reasoning but is created by God; the intellect is an instrument, not an autonomous cause.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate

The Hadith of the Lifted Pen: Who Is Obligated?
Clarifies legal obligation using the hadith and counterexample of the murahiqa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the hadith of the lifted pen to identify individuals who are not legally obligated (mukallaf) and explain why intellect alone is insufficient for taklif.

Core Idea
The pen is lifted from three: obligation requires both intellect and the arrival of revelation or puberty.

This passage applies the epistemological principles from the previous lesson to concrete legal cases. The hadith of the lifted pen is cited to show that a child (sabi) is not obligated to have faith, even if he possesses intellect. Similarly, an adult who has not received the call (da'wah) is excused. The example of a girl approaching puberty (murahiqa) illustrates how the ruling changes when she reaches puberty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its textual category
The hadith 'رفع القلم عن ثلاث' is a general (amm) statement indicating that three categories are not accountable. In Hanafi usul, amm is binding unless specified.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning (dalala) is qati regarding the lift of the pen.
2
Apply the hadith to the child (sabi)
The child before puberty is included in 'الصبي' (child). Since the pen is lifted, no obligations apply. The child's intellect does not make him mukallaf.
Contrast with Mu'tazila who say intellect alone suffices for obligation.
3
Examine the case of the murahiqa (girl near puberty)
The example of a murahiqa under a Muslim husband: she is not considered an apostate if she cannot describe Islam, because she is not yet obligated. But upon puberty, obligation begins and she separates if she cannot profess faith.
This shows that puberty (bulugh) is a trigger for taklif.
4
Apply to the adult who never received the call
An adult who has not received the message of Islam is not obligated by mere intellect. If he dies without believing, he is excused.
This is the Hanafi position, refuting the Mu'tazila who would deem him sinful.

باب القياس
اختلاف الناس في العقل
درك الحواس، فيبدو المطلوب للقلب فيدركه القلب بتأمله بتوفيق الله تعالى أي يظهر لا بإيجابه وهو كالشمس في الملكوت الظاهرة إذا بزغت وبدا شعاعها ووضح الطريق كانت العين مدركة بشهابها، بسبب ضوء الشمس الأشياء أي ظهر درك الحواس يعني العقل نور يتضح به طريق ابتدائه من موضع ينتهي إليه درك الحواس؛ لأن الإنسان إذا بصر بناء وانتهى إليه حسن البصر يدرك بعقله أن له بانياً ذا حياة وقدرة وعلم، فهذا طريق ابتداؤه من حيث انتهى إليه درك الحواس وهو البناء، وهذا الطريق اتضح بسبب العقل وهو : أي العقل في الملك الباطن الملكوت أي الملك والتاء زائدة للمبالغة كالجبروت والرغبوت :بزغت أي طلعت الشمس والجملة الشرطية تعليل لقوله: "وهو كالشمس بشهابها : أي بنورها من غير أن توجب الشمس رؤية تلك الأشياء، فكذا القلب يدرك ما هو غائب عن الحواس بنور العقل من غير أن يكون العقل موجباً لذلك. ف: اعلم أن في هذه العبارة إشارة إلى ردّ المعتزلة المخالفين لنا في مسألة النظر، وإني سأتلو عليك تفصيل المذاهب فيها، وأبين ما هو الحق فيها، فاعلم - أرشدك الله تعالى - أن عند الأشعري إفادة النظر العلم بالعادة لا دخل للنظر في الإفادة أصلاً ليس علة تامة ولا ناقصة، بل العلم يدور معه دوران أمر مع آخر، لا علاقة بينهما في الأكثر أو الدائم كوجود الإنسان مع الحمار، فلو كان الإنسان موجوداً بلا وجود حمار أو بالعكس فلا مضائقة؛ إذ لا مؤثر عنده إلا الله تعالى بمعنى أنه المستقل، لكنه فاعل مختار، فصدور المعلول عنه بلا وجوب منه كما ذهب إليه الفلاسفة؛ لأن الوجوب ينافي الاختيار، ولا وجوب عليه كما ذهب إليه المعتزلة والشيعة من وجوب اللطف عليه تعالى وأما عند المعتزلة فالإفادة بالتوليد، وهو عبارة عن إيجاد فعل بتوسط فعل آخر کحركة المفتاح بحركة اليد، وكالألم بعد الضرب، فإذا باشر النظر يحدث بعده العلم، كما إذا ضرب رجل رجلا فبمباشرة الضرب يحصل الألم بعده، وأما عند الحكماء فبطريق الإعداد، فإن النظر يعد الذهن إعدادا تاما، فيفيض عليه العلم من المبدأ الفياض وجوباً منه هذا تفصيل المذاهب والحق أن العلم واجب عقيب النظر وإن لم يكن واجبا منه تعالى غير متولد من النظر كما ذهب إليه المعتزلة.
أما الوجوب فلأن كل من علم أن العالم متغيّر وكل متغير حادث فمع حضور هذين العلمين في الذهن يستحيل أن لا يعلم أنه حادث، والعلم بهذا الامتناع ضروري، وأما إبطال التوليد فلأن العلم ممكن في نفسه وإن كان بعد النظر، وكل ممكن مقدور له تعالى، فيكون هو أيضا مقدورا الله تعالى، فيمتنع وقوعه بغير قدرته، وهذا هو مختار الإمام الرازي، وإليه ذهب القاضي أبو بكر الباقلاني وإمام الحرمين و به ارتضى صاحب المسلم،
وما بالعقل كفاية. ولهذا قلنا: إن الصبي غير مكلف بالإيمان، حتى إذا عقلت المراهقة وهي تحت مسلم بين أبوين مسلمين ولم تصف الإسلام لم تجعل مرتدة ولم تبن من زوجها ولو بلغت كذلك لبانت من زوجها وكذا نقول في الذي في العاقل البالغ لم تبلغه الدعوة: إنه غير مكلف بمجرد العقل، وإنه إذا لم يصف إيمانا ولا كفرا بالإيمان و لم يعتقد على شيء كان معذوراً
وقال شارحه مولانا نظام الدين له: فالأصلح الوجوب، وكون النظر علة قريبة والفياض هو الله تعالى، ولذلك يحكم العقل بالوجوب، ولم أجد هذا المعنى مخالفاً للنصوص الإلهية والنبوية. فتدبر في هذا المقام، فإنه من مزال الأقدام. كفاية: يعني وإن كان العقل آلة للإدراك ولكنه ليس بكاف في حصول المعرفة بغير توفيق الله تعالى. هذا ما قال بعض الشراح، والأولى أن يقال: إن العقل وإن كان يعرف قبح الأفعال وحسنها ولكنه ليس بمستبد في ذلك أي ليس بمستقل، حتى يتحقق الأحكام بمجرد العقل من غير ورود الشرع، كما هو مذهب المعتزلة. غير مكلف بالإيمان: أي الإيمان ليس بواجب عليه؛ لأن الوجوب وكذا سائر الأحكام بالخطاب لا بمجرد العقل، وهو غير مكلف لقوله عليه السلام: "رفع القلم عن ثلاث: عن النائم حتى يستيقظ، وعن الصبي حتى يبلغ، وعن المعتوه حتى يعقل". رواه الترمذي رقم: ١٤٢٣ وأبو داود والدارمي عن عائشة وابن ماجة عنها وأحمد، وصححه الحاكم، ولكنه لو آمن يصح إيمانه لوجود العقل، وعند الأشعرية إيمانه غير صحيح؛ إذ العقل لا يعبأ به عندهم، والاعتبار بالشرع، وفي حقه الشرع ليس موجود؛ لأنه غير مكلف، وعند المعتزلة لما كان العقل كافياً يجب عليه الإيمان وإن لم يرد به الشرع. المراهقة: هي المرأة التي قاربت البلوغ. وهي تحت مسلم إلخ بيان لإسلامها الحكمي بوجه لبانت من زوجها : يعني إذا كانت المرأة عاقلة ولكن لم تبلغ وهي تحت عبد مسلم، فاستوصف منها الإسلام ولم تقدر على البيان لا يحكم بردتها؛ لأن الردة خروج عن الإسلام وهي لم تكن مسلمة قبل لعدم قدرتها على وصف الإسلام، فلايحكم بردتها ولكن هي غير مكلفة بالإسلام بسبب عدم البلوغ؛ إذ العقل وإن كان موجوداً فيها لكنه غير كاف فإذا لم يجب عليها الإسلام لاتبين عن زوجها. نعم لو بلغت ووجب عليها الإسلام وهي بعد البلوغ أيضاً لاتقدر على وصف الإسلام لبانت من زوجها البتة وكذا أي كما قلنا في الصبي العاقل: إنه غير مكلف بالإيمان لعدم كفاية عقله تغيّر ورود الشرع في حقه بسبب عدم بلوغه كذا نقول في: إلخ. الله الدعوة: أي دعوة الرسول أو من قام مقامه بأن يكون على شاهق الجبل ولم يبق بعد البلوغ حتى يعينه بالتجربة ودرك العواقب كان معذوراً : هذا إذا مات بعد البلوغ من ساعته، فإذا لم تبلغه الدعوة ولم يأته مما هو قائم مقام الدعوة وزمان النظر والاستدلال على توحيده سبحانه وتعالى.

بوجه أكد.
Chapter of Qiyas. The disagreement of people regarding the intellect. The perception of the senses... the desired thing appears to the heart and the heart perceives it by reflecting upon it with the help of Allah Almighty, i.e., it appears, not by its necessitation. It is like the sun in the visible kingdom; when it rises and its rays appear and the path becomes clear, the eye perceives [objects] by its radiance, due to the light of the sun. The things appear. The perception of the senses means that the intellect is a light by which the path from its starting point to the point where the perception of the senses ends becomes clear. Because when a person sees a building and his sight reaches its end, he perceives with his intellect that it has a builder possessing life, power, and knowledge. This is a path whose starting point is where the perception of the senses ended, i.e., the building, and this path becomes clear due to the intellect. [The commentator says:] 'He' meaning the intellect in the inner kingdom, i.e., the kingdom, and the 'ta' is added for exaggeration like jabarut and raghbut. 'Bazaghat' means the sun rose, and the conditional sentence is an explanation of his statement: 'It is like the sun with its radiance,' i.e., by its light, without the sun necessitating the vision of those things. Similarly, the heart perceives what is absent from the senses by the light of the intellect, without the intellect being the necessitator of that. Know that in this expression there is an indication of refuting the Mu'tazila who oppose us in the matter of reasoning. I will recite to you the details of the schools of thought in it and clarify what is true in it. Know... that according to Ash'ari, reasoning produces knowledge by habit; reasoning has no role in production at all, it is neither a complete nor an incomplete cause. Rather, knowledge goes along with it as one thing goes with another, without any relation between them in most or always, like the existence of a human with a donkey. So if a human exists without a donkey existing or vice versa, there is no problem; because according to him there is no effect except Allah, meaning He alone is independent, and He is a free agent. So the effect proceeds from Him without necessity from Him, as the philosophers held, because necessity contradicts free choice. And there is no obligation upon Him as the Mu'tazila and Shi'a held regarding the obligation of grace upon Him. According to the Mu'tazila, production is by generation (tawlid), which is the creation of an act by means of another act, like the movement of a key by the movement of a hand, and like pain after a blow. So when one engages in reasoning, knowledge arises after it, just as when a man strikes a man, by directly striking, pain occurs after it. According to the philosophers, it is by way of preparation (i'dad); reasoning prepares the mind fully, then knowledge flows upon it from the Emanating Principle necessarily from Him. This is the detail of the schools. The truth is that knowledge is necessary (wajib) after reasoning, although it is not necessary from Him [i.e., His action is not compelled], nor is it generated from reasoning as the Mu'tazila held. As for the necessity, because everyone who knows that the world is changing and everything changing is originated (hadith), when these two pieces of knowledge are present in the mind, it is impossible that he does not know that it is originated, and knowledge of this impossibility is necessary. As for invalidating generation, because knowledge is possible in itself although it comes after reasoning, and everything possible is subject to the power of Allah, so it is also within the power of Allah, and it is impossible for it to occur without His power. This is the choice of Imam al-Razi, and Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani and Imam al-Haramayn agreed, and the author of al-Muslim approved. And by the intellect is not sufficiency. Therefore we said: the child (sabi) is not obligated to have faith (iman), so that if a girl approaching puberty (murahiqa) who is under a Muslim husband between two Muslim parents cannot describe Islam, she is not considered an apostate and does not separate from her husband. But if she reaches puberty similarly, she separates from her husband. Similarly, we say regarding the one who is an adult of sound mind who has not received the call: he is not obligated by mere intellect, and if he does not describe faith nor disbelief by faith and does not believe in anything, he is excused. And his commentator, our master Nizam al-Din, said: the most correct is the necessity, and that reasoning is a proximate cause and the Emanator is Allah, therefore the intellect rules with necessity, and I have not found this meaning contradictory to the divine and prophetic texts. So reflect on this station, for it is a slippery place. 'Sufficiency': means although the intellect is an instrument of perception, it is not sufficient for obtaining knowledge without the help of Allah. This is what some commentators said. The better view is to say: the intellect, although it knows the evil and good of actions, is not independent in that, i.e., not autonomous, so that rulings are realized by mere intellect without the arrival of the Sharia, as is the doctrine of the Mu'tazila. 'Not obligated to faith': i.e., faith is not obligatory upon him; because obligation and all other rulings are by address (khitab), not by mere intellect. And he is not obligated due to his statement: 'The pen is lifted from three: from the sleeper until he wakes, from the child until he reaches puberty, and from the insane until he becomes sane.' Narrated by Tirmidhi no. 1423, Abu Dawud, al-Darimi from Aisha, Ibn Majah from her, and Ahmad, and authenticated by al-Hakim. But if he believes, his faith is valid due to the presence of intellect. According to the Ash'aris, his faith is not valid; because they give no weight to intellect, and the consideration is with the Sharia, and in his case the Sharia is not present because he is not obligated. According to the Mu'tazila, since the intellect is sufficient, faith becomes obligatory upon him even if the Sharia does not come. 'Murahiqa': she is the woman close to puberty. 'She is under a Muslim' etc. is an explanation of her legal Islam in a certain way, 'she separates from her husband' means if the woman is intelligent but has not reached puberty and she is under a Muslim husband, and she is asked to describe Islam and cannot do so, she is not judged to be an apostate; because apostasy is leaving Islam, and she was not Muslim before due to her inability to describe Islam, so she is not judged to be an apostate. But she is not obligated to Islam due to not reaching puberty; for even though intellect is present in her, it is not sufficient. So if Islam is not obligatory upon her, she does not separate from her husband. Indeed, if she reaches puberty and Islam becomes obligatory upon her, and even after puberty she still cannot describe Islam, she definitely separates from her husband. Similarly, as we said regarding the intelligent child: he is not obligated to faith due to the insufficiency of his intellect and the change of the arrival of the Sharia in his case due to his not reaching puberty. Similarly, we say regarding: etc. 'The call': i.e., the call of the Messenger or whoever stands in his place, such as being on a mountain top and there remains no one after puberty to assist him through experience and understanding of consequences. 'He is excused': this is if he dies after puberty immediately. So if the call has not reached him and nothing has come to him that stands in the place of the call and the time of reasoning and inferring the oneness of Allah, the Most High, he is excused. With emphasis.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the epistemological role of the intellect (aql) in acquiring knowledge, particularly knowledge of God, and its legal ramifications for obligation (taklif). The author begins by describing the intellect as a light that enables the heart to perceive what is beyond the senses, similar to how sunlight enables vision. He then contrasts four schools of thought on how knowledge arises from reasoning (nazar): the Ash'aris hold that reasoning produces knowledge only by custom (adah) and God is the sole agent; the Mu'tazila claim that reasoning generates knowledge directly (tawlid); the philosophers assert that reasoning prepares the mind and knowledge flows necessarily from the First Principle; and the truth according to the author (following Imam al-Razi) is that knowledge is necessary (wajib) after reasoning, but it is neither caused by reasoning nor necessitated from God—it is within God's power. The author refutes generation (tawlid) by arguing that knowledge is possible, and every possible is within God's power, so it cannot occur without His power. He then applies this principle to legal obligation: the intellect alone does not impose obligations. A child (sabi) is not obligated to have faith, as evidenced by the hadith that the pen is lifted from three categories. The example of a girl approaching puberty (murahiqa) under a Muslim husband illustrates that she is not considered an apostate if she cannot describe Islam, because she is not yet obligated. If she reaches puberty and still cannot describe it, she becomes an apostate. Similarly, an adult who has not received the call of Islam is not obligated by mere intellect and is excused. The commentator Mulla Nizam al-Din adds that the intellect can rule with necessity but only as a proximate cause, and that this view does not contradict revelation. The correct doctrine is that the intellect is neither autonomous nor sufficient; obligation results from divine address (khitab), not reason alone. This refutes the Mu'tazila who deem intellect sufficient and the Ash'aris who dismiss it entirely.

Key Terms
مكلف (mukallaf): A person who is legally responsible for performing religious duties; required to have faith and practice Islam.
رفع القلم (raf' al-qalam): The lifting of the pen of accountability, meaning actions are not recorded as obligations or sins.
مراهقة (murahiqa): A girl approaching puberty, close to the age of legal responsibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling for an adult who has never received the call of Islam (da'wah) and dies without believing?
A) He is sinful and punished for disbelief.
B) He is excused and not punished.
C) His faith would be invalid if he believed, so he is still punished.
D) He is considered Muslim by nature.

Key Takeaway
Obligation (taklif) requires both intellect and the arrival of the divine address; the hadith of the lifted pen establishes that children and those unreached by revelation are excused.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Intellect and Legal Obligation Without Da'wa
Usul dispute on intellect vs. da'wa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi position that intellect alone is insufficient for taklif without da'wa, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf with the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Intellect alone cannot obligate; a period of reflection stands in place of the prophetic call.

This passage delves into a foundational dispute in Usul al-Fiqh: is rational capacity sufficient to impose legal obligation (taklif) absent a prophetic message? The Hanafi school, through Abu Hanifa's analogy of the safih (foolish person), argues that a specified period of reflection substitutes for the da'wa, making the person liable if they fail to believe. This lesson unpacks the proof, the critique of opposing views, and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the contested issue
Identify the central question: Is intellect alone sufficient for legal obligation (taklif) without the prophetic call (da'wa)?
2
Identify the Hanafi position and its core analogy
The Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa) holds that intellect alone is not sufficient; a period of reflection is needed, analogous to the 25-year waiting period for the safih. This is based on Quran 4:6, where indefinite 'prudence' includes presumptive prudence.
The safih's wealth is withheld until 25 years, establishing a fixed period as a substitute for actual prudence.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i counter-position
The Shafi'i school holds that intellect and a substitute for the call (e.g., natural reflection) are sufficient. Thus, an intelligent adult without da'wa is liable for blood-money if killed.
The passage notes an internal contradiction: Shafi'i negates intellect by using intellectual proofs.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response argues that intellect is prone to whim and error, so it cannot be an independent proof. Thus, neither the Mu'tazila (making intellect an obligating cause) nor the Shafi'i (negating it entirely) have decisive evidence.
Both extremes lack a decisive proof (dhalil qati').
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: If an intelligent adult without da'wa commits murder, the Shafi'i school imposes liability (qisas/diyah), while the Hanafi school does not because obligation requires the da'wa or its substitute.
This affects rulings on crimes and punishment in cases with no revelation.

بنفسه بحال.
Chapter of Qiyas: Disagreement of people regarding intellect. If God aids him with experience and grants him time to perceive consequences, he is not excused even if the call did not reach him, as Abu Hanifa stated in the case of the foolish person when he reaches twenty-five years: his wealth is not withheld from him; because he has completed the period of experience and testing, so he must necessarily increase in prudence. There is no decisive proof for those who make intellect a cause and for those who negate it. And there is no decisive proof in this chapter. So whoever makes intellect an obligating cause that the Law cannot contradict has no proof to rely on. And whoever negates it entirely also has no proof. This is the school of al-Shafi'i, for he said regarding a people who have not received the call: if they are killed, liability is incurred, even if the call did not reach them, because faith became obligatory upon them due to the existence of two matters: one is intellect, and the second is that which stands in the place of the call. This is similar to what was said: etc. His wealth is not withheld from him: even if prudence is not perceived from him, although handing over wealth to him is linked to perceiving prudence as God said: 'If you perceive from them prudence, then give them their wealth.' The period is established in place of prudence, and even if prudence is not actualized, we say it exists presumptively. This suffices for handing over wealth because He said 'prudence' with the indefinite, meaning if you see any prudence, whether actual or presumptive. Just as the period is established in place of prudence, so the time of reflection and inference for the mentioned person is established in place of the call. So if he does not believe after intellect and what stands in place of the call, he is punished. When it was objected regarding the issue of the foolish person that you assigned twenty-five years, while analogy would require assigning three days by analogy with the apostate, he answered: there is no decisive text specifying the limit. For the period of grace is not a decisive text such that it could be said its duration is three days or more; because intellect varies in its original constitution, so some intelligent people may be guided in a short time while others are not guided even over a long period. So whoever makes intellect an independent proof so that rulings are realized without revelation of the Law and denies the existence of the Law in opposition to it, as the Mu'tazila hold, has no proof to rely on, and what they argue is flawed and rejected. They have no rational or transmitted proof that yields even probability, let alone certainty. And this is the school of al-Shafi'i: according to al-Shafi'i, if someone kills an intelligent adult who has not received the call, liability for blood-money is upon the killer; because the victim, even if the call did not reach him, although he was intelligent and adult and could infer the oneness of God, he is not excused. So he makes their disbelief forgiven, because he does not find in the Law that intellect is not considered for establishing capacity; rather, he negates it by intellectual proofs and reasoning, thus contradicting his own position. And intellect is never free from whim, so it is not valid by itself at all.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute regarding whether intellect (عقل) alone suffices for legal obligation (تكليف) in the absence of the prophetic call (دعوة). The author critiques both extremes: those who make intellect an independent cause (the Mu'tazila) and those who negate it entirely (the Ash'ari/Shafi'i position). The Hanafi position, as exemplified by Abu Hanifa's ruling on the foolish person (سفيه) who reaches 25 years, is that a specified period of experience stands in place of prudence, and similarly a period of reflection stands in place of the call. Thus, punishment is possible if reflection does not lead to faith. The author refutes the Shafi'i view that intellect and a substitute for the call are sufficient, and also refutes the Mu'tazila's claim that intellect is an independent proof. The conclusion is that both sides lack decisive evidence, and intellect alone is not a valid basis for obligation or excuse.

Key Terms
العقل (al-'aql): Intellect; the rational faculty that distinguishes humans and enables understanding and inference.
الدعوة (al-da'wa): The prophetic call or message (risala) that conveys the commands of God.

The Hanafi school uses the analogy of the safih and Quran 4:6 to establish that a period of reflection stands in place of the prophetic call, rendering the intelligent adult liable after sufficient time.

Apostasy of a Minor: Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Dispute over whether a minor's apostasy is valid in worldly rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the validity of a minor's apostasy in worldly rulings and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using usul principles.

Core Idea
A minor's apostasy is valid in all rulings except execution, as its gravity precludes pardon.

This lesson examines a classical ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on one side and Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i on the other regarding whether a minor's apostasy produces worldly legal effects. The dispute hinges on the principle of raf' al-qalam (lifting of the pen) versus the nature of apostasy as an unforgivable act. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply usul principles to divergent rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and the opposing position (Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i) regarding the effectiveness of a minor's apostasy in worldly rulings.
Both sides agree on afterlife consequences; the dispute is about this-worldly effects.
2
Locate each side's dalil
For the Hanafis: apostasy is a grave act that does not admit of pardon. For the opponents: the pen is lifted from minors, so they are not liable for harmful acts.
The Hanafi dalil focuses on the nature of the act; the opponent's dalil focuses on the subject's capacity.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The worldly effects (like separation of marriage) are not intended purposes but necessary consequences (hawadim) of the apostasy's validity. Pardon (afw) cannot apply to such an act.
The text uses 'hukman li-sihhatihi la qasdan ilayhi' – a ruling due to its validity, not intentionally.
4
Explore the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify practical differences: under the Hanafi position, a minor apostate's marriage dissolves and he cannot inherit; under the opponent's position, these remain intact until puberty.
These consequences follow directly from the core disagreement.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text implies that the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is the correct one because the effects are automatic and cannot be pardoned.
Consider how the weight of evidence (gravity of apostasy vs. protection of minors) is balanced.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الردة فلا تحتمل العفو في أحكام الآخرة، وما يلزمه من
أي على الصبي
أحكام الدنيا عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف والشافعي له، فإنما يلزمه حكما لصحته لا قصداً

And as for apostasy, it does not admit of pardon in the rulings of the afterlife, and what attaches to him — i.e., the minor — of the rulings of this world according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) contrary to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, it attaches to him as a ruling due to its validity, not intentionally, so pardon for the like of it is not valid, just as when it is established as a consequence of his parents.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute regarding the apostasy of a minor. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if a minor apostatizes, his apostasy is valid in both worldly and afterlife rulings: his wife becomes separated, he cannot inherit from Muslim relatives, and if he dies upon apostasy, he will be eternally in Hell. However, he is not executed because the condition of warfare before puberty is absent. If someone kills him, the killer's blood is wasted (no liability). Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i hold that a minor's apostasy is not effective in worldly rulings because it is pure harm, and a minor is protected from harm (the pen is lifted). The text explains that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's position imposes these worldly effects as a necessary consequence (bi hukm al-sihha) of the apostasy being valid, not as the intended purpose (la qasdan). Thus, pardon (afw) cannot apply to such a grave act. The analogy of following parents to dar al-harb is given: if a minor's parents apostatize and join enemy territory, the minor is treated similarly.

Key Terms
الردة (al-riddah): Apostasy: renunciation of Islam by a Muslim.
الصبي (al-sabi): A minor who has not reached puberty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The marriage is annulled only if he remains apostate after puberty.

Key Takeaway
A minor's apostasy is legally effective in all rulings except execution, because the act's gravity overrides the general protection of minors from penal liability.

The Apostasy of a Minor: Between Necessity and Intent
Dispute on validity of apostasy for a minor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates the apostasy of a minor and apply the distinction between direct intent and necessary consequences in legal reasoning.

Core Idea
A minor's apostasy is valid because its harmful consequences are necessary entailments, not intended objectives.

This passage delves into a classic usul dispute: can a minor's apostasy carry worldly legal consequences? The Hanafi school, represented by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, argues yes, while Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i disagree. At stake is the distinction between direct intent and necessary implications in legal causation (talil).

Guided Path
1
State the contested issue
Identify the precise legal question: whether the apostasy of a minor (who had previously embraced Islam) is valid for worldly rulings such as marriage dissolution and inheritance.
2
Identify the Hanafi position and its proof
State the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: the minor's apostasy is valid in all respects. The proof is that just as his faith was valid as a benefit, the opposite (apostasy) must also be valid, and the harmful consequences are necessary entailments (lawazim), not the intended purpose.
The proof relies on talil and analogy with a minor following his parents' apostasy.
3
Identify the opposing position and its proof
State the view of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i: the apostasy has no worldly effect because it is pure harm and the minor is under the lifting of the pen (raf' al-qalam) – not accountable for harmful acts.
The opposing proof emphasizes the protective status of the minor.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Explain the Hanafi rebuttal: the harm is not intended directly (la qasdan) but is an inseparable consequence of the validity of apostasy. The ruling of validity is based on the necessity of treating his action as legally significant, just as his faith was.
This distinguishes between penal accountability and civil/status effects.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the minor's marriage dissolves and he cannot inherit from Muslims. According to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, his marriage and inheritance rights remain intact.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الأمور المعترضة أحكام الدنيا عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف له، فإنما يلزمه حكما لصحته لا قصداً أي عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد والشافعي إليه، فلم يصح العفو عن مثله كما إذا ثبت تبعاً لأبويه. [أنواع الأمور المعترضة] الارتداد فصل في الأمور المعترضة على الأهلية العوارض نوعان: سماوي ومكتسب، أما السماوي فهو منرا عشراً وهو ضد السماوي من غيره كالكفر، وكان الأولى أن يذكر المصنّف هذا القسم بعد القسم الأول، والحاصل أن هذا القسم من الأفعال يعتبر من الصبي لو ارتد - والعياذ بالله تعالى - تعتبر ردته عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد بحملها في حق أحكام الدنيا والآخرة حتى تبين منه امرأته ولا يرث من أقاربه المسلمين، ولو مات على ارتداده كان مخلدا في النار كذا في النهاية، ولكن لا يقتل؛ لأنه لم توجد منه المحاربة قبل البلوغ، ولو قتله أحد يهدر دمه ولا يجب على القاتل شيء، وقال أبو يوسف والشافعي حملها لا تعتبر ردته في حق أحكام الدنيا؛ لأنها ضرر محض، وإنما حكمنا بصحة إيمانه لكونه نفعاً محضاً، ولما كان يرد أن المضار مدفوع عنه؛ لأنه مرفوع القلم بمعنى أن المضار مدفوع عنه؛ لأنه مرفوع القلم بمعنى أنه لا يحاسب خطاياه، والقول بصحة ارتداده يؤدي إلى إثبات الضرر في حقه حيث تبين امرأته المسلمة ويحرم عن ميراث أقاربه المسلمين، أجاب عنه بقوله: وما يلزمه إلى أحكام الدنيا من البينونة بينه وبين امرأته المسلمة وحرمان الميراث. لا قصداً إليه: والضمير راجع إلى ما يعني لزوم هذه الأحكام من ضرورة الحكم بصحة ارتداده؛ لأنها لوازمها، لا أن يكون الحكم بصحة الارتداد لأجل هذه الأحكام والحاصل أن ما يلزم من المضار يثبت ضمناً في حكم صحة الردة لا قصدا مثله أي مثل الارتداد فالمعنى لا يصح العفو عن مثل هذا الأمر العظيم الذي لا يحتمل العفو بوجه بواسطة لزوم هذه الأحكام. تبعاً لأبويه: بأن ارتدا ولحقا بدار الحرب، فإنه تلزمه هذه الأحكام ولايمتنع ثبوته بواسطة لزومها، فكذا في ما نحن فيه
Section on impediments. The rulings of this world according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) contrary to Abu Yusuf, for he (Abu Yusuf) said: It only becomes binding as a ruling due to its validity, not intentionally. That is, according to Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i (but Abu Yusuf disagreed). So forgiveness of the like of this is not valid, as when it is established through following one's parents. [Types of impediments] Apostasy. Section on impediments to legal capacity: impediments are two types: heavenly and acquired. As for heavenly, they are ten... and it is the opposite of heavenly from other than him like disbelief. It would have been better for the author to mention this section after the first section. The summary is that this type of action is considered from the child if he apostatizes (God forbid). His apostasy is considered by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad as binding in terms of the rulings of this world and the Hereafter, so his wife becomes separated from him, and he does not inherit from his Muslim relatives. If he dies in his apostasy, he will be eternally in Hellfire, as in al-Nihaya. But he is not killed because he did not engage in combat before puberty. If someone kills him, his blood is wasted and nothing is owed to the killer. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said: His apostasy is not considered regarding the rulings of this world because it is pure harm, and we only rule on the validity of his faith because it is pure benefit. Since it is argued that harms are warded off from him because the pen is lifted, meaning that his sins are not accounted for, the statement of the validity of his apostasy leads to establishing harm against him where his Muslim wife becomes separated and he is deprived of inheritance from his Muslim relatives. He answered by saying: What is binding upon him regarding worldly rulings of separation from his Muslim wife and deprivation of inheritance is not intended. The pronoun refers to the meaning: these rulings are necessary consequences of the ruling of the validity of his apostasy, not that the ruling of apostasy is for the sake of these rulings. The summary: that which results of harm is established implicitly in the ruling of the validity of apostasy, not intentionally. The like of it, i.e., like apostasy, so the meaning is: it is not valid to forgive such a great matter that does not admit forgiveness in any way through the necessity of these rulings. As following one's parents: if they apostatize and join the abode of war, then these rulings are binding upon him, and their establishment is not prevented through their necessity. So too in our case.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed usul dispute regarding the apostasy of a minor (sabi). The matn likely stated that the apostasy of a minor is effective in worldly and afterlife rulings according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The commentator expands on this by citing the opposing views of Abu Yusuf (within the Hanafi school) and Imam al-Shafi'i, who argue that since the minor is not legally accountable (raf' al-qalam), his apostasy should not carry worldly consequences that are purely harmful. The Hanafi response is that the harmful consequences (such as dissolution of marriage and loss of inheritance) are not the intended purpose but are necessary entailments (lawazim) of the validity of the apostasy itself. The commentator also draws an analogy: just as a minor's apostasy following his parents' apostasy results in similar rulings without being prevented, so too in the case of his independent apostasy. This is a classic example of the use of talil (causal reasoning) and the distinction between direct intent and necessary consequences in Hanafi legal theory.

Key Terms
ردة (riddah): Apostasy from Islam; considered one of the impediments (awāriḍ) that affect legal capacity.
صبي (ṣabī): Minor child who has not reached puberty; in this context, one who had embraced Islam as a child.
مرفوع القلم (marfūʿ al-qalam): Lifting of the pen (legal responsibility) from the minor, meaning his actions are not recorded for punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The marriage remains valid.
B) The wife becomes separated from him.
C) The marriage is suspended until he reaches puberty.
D) The marriage requires a new contract.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates a minor's apostasy by treating the harmful outcomes as necessary consequences, not as intended penalties.

Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute on the Capacity of the Ma'dhun Slave: Distinguishing Possession from Ownership
Presents the Shafi'i argument against slave's transaction capacity and Hanafi rebuttal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the usul principle underlying the Hanafi distinction between milk al-yad and milk al-raqaba, and apply it to derive the ma'dhun slave's capacity for transaction.

Core Idea
Transaction primarily effects possession (yad), not ownership of capital (raqaba); thus a slave can transact without owning the capital.

In this passage, the Hanafi school presents a sophisticated rebuttal to Imam al-Shafi'i's argument that a ma'dhun slave (a slave authorized to trade) cannot legally transact because he cannot own capital. By carefully distinguishing between the purpose of a transaction (possession for survival) and its incidental consequence (ownership of capital), the Hanafi position affirms the slave's capacity to acquire possession while recognizing that capital ownership remains with the master. This lesson unpacks the doctrinal dispute and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school affirms: the ma'dhun slave can transact in an original capacity and has possession (yad) over his earnings, but ownership of capital (milk al-raqaba) belongs to the master.
The slave acts as an original, not a representative.
2
State the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that if the slave could transact, he would be capable of owning the capital, since transaction causes ownership. Consensus says he cannot own, so transaction is void.
This is a qiyas argument: cause and effect must align.
3
Identify the usul principle behind each argument
The Shafi'i view assumes transaction necessarily leads to ownership of the capital (milk al-raqaba). The Hanafi view separates the primary purpose (milk al-yad) from the means (milk al-raqaba). The principle is: the absence of the means does not negate the end if another means exists.
This involves the concept of 'maqsūd aṣlī' (primary purpose) vs. 'wasīla' (means).
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal's key distinction
The Hanafi rebuttal asserts that the primary purpose of transaction is possession (milk al-yad), which the slave can attain. Ownership of capital is merely a means to that end, and the master stands in place of the slave for that means. Thus, the slave's inability to own capital does not prevent transaction.
The analogy to a wakil (agent) supports this: a wakil transacts but does not own the capital.
5
Apply the principle to practical examples
The text gives two scenarios: (1) during the master's illness, the slave's transactions are treated like a wakil's, only valid from one-third of the estate; (2) if a ma'dhun slave authorizes his own slave and the master revokes, the sub-agent is not automatically revoked, as in wakala.
These examples show the Hanafi view treats the slave like a wakil in matters of capital ownership and continuity of permission.

وهذا عندنا أي كون العبد أهلا للتصرف في المال أحد ضربي مذهبنا يتصرف بطريق الأصالة لا بطريق النيابة، ويثبت له اليد على إكسابه وهو اليد: وأما ملك الرقبة فهو بالنسبة إلى ملك اليد من الزوائد، وفيه دفع لما احتج به الشافعي على مذهبه، وهو أن تصرفه لنفسه ليس بأهليته بل بطريق الاستفادة من المولى كالوكيل ويده على أكسابه يد أمانة كالمودع. تقرير الاحتجاج أنه لو كان أهلا للتصريف لكان أهلا للملك؛ إذ التصرف سبب لملك الرقبة، والسبب لا يوجد بعد حكمه، والملك لا يثبت له إجماعاً، فكذا التصرف؛ لأن انتفاء اللازم وهو هنا الملك يستلزم انتفاء الملزوم وهو التصرف، وإذا لم يثبت له التصرف لم يكن أهلا لاستحقاق اليد؛ لأن اليد إنما يستفاد بملك التصرف أو اليد. وتقرير الدفع أن المقصود الأصلي من التصرف ملك اليد، وهو حاصل للعبد؛ لأن الإنسان يحتاج إلى ما هو سبب لبقائه، ولا يمكن ذلك إلا بكونه في يده. وأما ملك الرقبة فهو ليس بلازم وسبب له، وهو مقصود أصلي بل هو وسيلة إليه، وعدم أهلية العبد للوسيلة الحاصلة لا يوجب عدم المقصود؛ إذ يمكن أن يكون له وسيلة أخرى. وهو الملك المشروع إلخ: أي يكون المولى قائماً مقام العبد في ملك الرقبة الذي هو وسيلة إلى الملك اليد الذي هو مقصود لعدم أهلية العبد له. ولهذا أي ولأن الملك لا يثبت للعبد لعدم أهليته بل يخلفه المولى جعلنا العبد في ملك التصرف، وملك اليد مستقل وأصل ولكنه في حكم الملك أي ملك الرقبة، وفي حكم بقاء الإذن كالوكيل أي غير مستقل؛ لأنه ليس أهلا لملك الرقبة، حتى لو اشترى شيئاً يقع الملك للمولى، فكان هو كالوكيل فللمولى حق الحجر عليه بعد الإذن بغير رضاه، كما للمؤكل حق عزل الوكيل بدون رضاه. "في حكم الملك" في مسائل إلخ متعلق بقوله "في حكم الملك". وفي عامة مسائل المأذون متعلق بقوله بقاء الإذن. والحاصل أنا جعلناه في حكم الملك في مسائل مرض المولى وفي حق بقاء الإذن في أكثر مسائل المأذون كالوكيل. صورة القسم الأول هي أن المولى أذن لعبده في التجارة، فكل ما باع العبد أو اشترى بغبن فاحش أو يسير في زمان مرض المولى لا يصح مطلقاً إن كان على المولى دين لتعلق حق الغرماء به، وإن لم يكن عليه دين يعتبر من ثلث ماله عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله لا من جميع المال لتعلق حق الورثاء به؛ لأنه بمنزلة الوكيل والملك للمولى، وصار كأن المولى باشر بنفسه، فيعتبر من الثلث ويتغير ما فعل المأذون كما يتغير فعل الوكيل في حالة مرض الموكل. وأما المحاباة بغبن فاحش فباطلة عند محمد وأبي يوسف رحمهما الله. ولو كان هذا التصرف في حال الصحة يصح ويعتبر من جميع مال المولى ولا يكون العبد في حال صحة المولى كالوكيل. وصورة القسم الثاني: هي أن العبد المأذون أذن لعبده في التجارة، ثم حجر المولى على المأذون الأول لا ينحجر الأول كالوكيل إذا وكل غيره، وقد قال له المؤكل اعمل برأيك، ثم عزل المؤكل الوكيل الأول لا ينعزل الثاني. نعم لو مات المولى صارا محجورين كما لو مات المؤكل صارا معزولين. ففي هذه المسألة ونظائرها جعل العبد.
And this in our [school] is that the slave is capable of disposition over wealth: one of the two types of our school, he acts in an original capacity, not by representation, and possession (yad) over his earnings is established for him, which is the yad. As for ownership of capital (milk al-raqaba), it is, relative to possession (milk al-yad), among the accessories. And in it is a refutation of what al-Shafi'i argued for his school, which is that his transaction for himself is not due to his own capacity but by derivation from the master like a wakil, and his hand over his earnings is a hand of trust (yad amana) like a depositor (mūda'). The summary of the argument [of al-Shafi'i] is that if he were capable of transacting, he would be capable of owning, because transaction is a cause for ownership of capital, and the cause is not found after its effect, and ownership is not established for him by consensus, so likewise transaction; because the absence of the necessary consequence, which here is ownership, necessitates the absence of the cause, which is transaction. And if transaction is not established for him, he is not eligible for acquisition of yad, because yad is only acquired by ownership of transaction or yad. And the summary of the rebuttal [by Hanafi] is that the primary purpose of transaction is possession (milk al-yad), and it is attained for the slave, because the human needs what is a cause for his survival, and that is not possible except by being in his hand. As for ownership of capital (milk al-raqaba), it is not a necessary consequence nor a cause for it, and it is not a primary purpose, but rather a means to it, and the slave's inability for the means does not necessitate the absence of the purpose; for it is possible that he has another means. And that is the prescribed ownership etc., meaning: the master stands in place of the slave in ownership of capital, which is a means to possession (yad) which is the purpose, due to the slave's inability. And for this reason, because ownership is not established for the slave due to his lack of capacity, but the master replaces him, we made the slave in the matter of ownership of disposition and possession independent and original, but he is in the ruling of ownership (i.e., ownership of capital) and in the ruling of continuation of permission like a wakil, i.e., not independent, because he is not capable of ownership of capital, so that if he buys something, the ownership falls to the master. He is like a wakil, and the master has the right to forbid him after permission without his consent, just as the principal has the right to dismiss the wakil without his consent. 'In the ruling of ownership' in certain issues is attached to his statement 'in the ruling of ownership'. And in general issues of the ma'dhun, it is attached to his statement 'continuation of permission'. The conclusion is that we made him in the ruling of ownership in issues of the master's illness and in the right of continuation of permission in most issues of the ma'dhun like a wakil. The example of the first type: the master gave his slave permission for trade; everything the slave sold or bought with a gross or slight disadvantage during the master's illness is not valid at all if the master has debts, because of the creditors' claim; if he has no debts, it is considered from one-third of his property according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, not from all the property, because of the heirs' claim, since he is like a wakil and the ownership is for the master, and it becomes as if the master did it himself, so it is considered from the third and what the ma'dhun does changes as the wakil's action changes in the case of the principal's illness. As for favor with a gross disadvantage, it is void according to Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on them. And if this transaction was during health, it is valid and considered from all the master's property, and the slave is not like a wakil when the master is healthy. The example of the second type: the ma'dhun slave gave permission to his own slave to trade, then the master forbade the first ma'dhun—the first is not forbidden, like a wakil who appoints another agent, and the principal said to him 'act with your opinion', then the principal dismissed the first wakil, the second is not dismissed. Yes, if the master died, both become forbidden, just as if the principal died, both become dismissed. So in this issue and its analogues, the slave [is treated]...
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (ikhtilaf) between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the legal capacity of a ma'dhun slave (a slave authorized to trade). The text first states the Hanafi position: the slave acts for himself (as an original, not as a representative), and he has the right of possession (yad) over his earnings, but ownership of capital (milk al-raqaba) belongs to the master. The Shafi'i argument is then presented: if the slave could transact, he would own the capital, but he cannot own by consensus, so his transactions are void and he does not even have possession. The Hanafi rebuttal distinguishes between the primary purpose of transaction (possession for survival) and the means (ownership of capital). The slave's inability to own capital does not prevent him from possessing the object of transaction; the master takes ownership of the capital on his behalf. The text then applies this principle to practical examples: if the master falls ill, the slave's transactions are treated like those of a wakil during the principal's illness—they are only valid up to one-third of the master's property if he has no debts, and invalid if he has debts. If the master is healthy, transactions are valid from all the property. Another example: if a ma'dhun slave authorizes his own slave to trade, and then the master revokes the first slave's permission, the second slave is not automatically revoked, similar to a wakil's sub-agency. This shows that the Hanafi school treats the ma'dhun slave as having independent capacity for possession but treats him like a wakil in matters of capital ownership and continuity of permission.

Key Terms
المأذون (al-ma'dhun): A slave authorized by his master to engage in trade.
ملك اليد (milk al-yad): Possession or ownership of the thing in hand, as opposed to ownership of the capital (raqaba).
ملك الرقبة (milk al-raqaba): Ownership of the capital or principal of a property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rebuttal against al-Shafi'i, what is the primary purpose (maqsūd aṣlī) of a transaction?
A) Ownership of capital (milk al-raqaba)
B) Possession (milk al-yad)
C) Profit
D) Transfer of ownership

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the ma'dhun slave has capacity for possession (yad) but not ownership of capital (raqaba), because transaction primarily yields possession, not ownership.

Slavery, Legal Authority, and the Exception for the Permitted Slave's Aman
Explaining that slavery cuts off all authority except the aman of a permitted slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that slavery cuts off authority (wilaya) and identify the exception for the permitted slave's aman, distinguishing between Abu Hanifa's position and that of Muhammad and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Slavery is a legal incapacity that removes all authority; only the permitted slave's aman is valid because he shares in spoils.

In this passage, we explore the foundational Hanafi principle that slavery constitutes a legal incapacity (ajz hukmi) that severs all forms of authority (wilaya). However, an important exception is made for the aman (safe conduct) given by a permitted slave (ma'dhun) during jihad. This exception is not based on the slave having authority, but rather on his partnership in the spoils, which makes his aman binding on himself first and then extending to others. The passage then presents a key usul dispute: does the generality of the hadith 'the covenant of the Muslims is one' allow any slave to give aman, or is it restricted to the permitted slave? We will see how Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i differ, and how the Hanafi school justifies its position through specification (takhsis).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on slavery and wilaya
Identify the general rule: slavery cuts off all types of authority because it is a legal incapacity. A slave cannot have authority over himself, so he cannot have authority over others.
Authority here includes judiciary, testimony, marriage, etc.
2
Identify the exception for the permitted slave's aman
The aman of a permitted slave (ma'dhun) is valid. Understand why: the permitted slave becomes a partner in the spoils (radhkh), so by giving aman he first forfeits his own right to spoils, and that ruling extends to others. This is not an act of authority but a consequence of his stake.
This is analogous to a slave's testimony on the hilal of Ramadan: he makes fasting binding on himself first.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Muhammad and al-Shafi'i argue that any Muslim slave can give valid aman. Their evidence: the hadith 'The covenant of the Muslims is one; the lowest of them can give binding aman' and the practice of 'Umar who allowed aman from a slave.
They take the hadith at its apparent generality (zahir).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa restricts the hadith to the permitted slave. Why? The unpermitted slave does not have a right to radhkh, so his aman would not be binding on himself first. The general hadith must be specified by this underlying principle.
This is a classic example of takhsis (specification) of a general text by a specific legal reasoning.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, only the aman of a permitted slave is valid; under Muhammad and al-Shafi'i, any Muslim slave's aman is valid.
This affects the rules of safe conduct in jihad and the rights of Muslims and non-Muslims.

أنه
وقال الترمذي: وقد روي عن عمر بن الخطاب أنه أجاز أمان العبد ، وروي عن النبي أنه قال: "ذمة المسلمين واحدة، يسعى بها أدناهم [الترمذي رقم: ۱۰۷۹] ومعنى هذا عند أهل العلم أن من أعطي الأمان من المسلمين فهو جائز على كلهم. أقول: هذا يدلّ على أذن العبد سواء كان مأذوناً أو لا، شرط أن يكون مؤمناً يجوز من
