أمانه، كما ذهب إليه محمد والشافعي حملها، وخص أبو حنيفة محله المأذون، فعلى هذا المراد من العبد المأذون لما مر. مثل شهادته أي هذا الأمان مثل شهادة العبد بهلال رمضان حييث يصح شهادته وليست من الولاية، بل باعتبار أن العبد ألزم الصوم بنفسه أولاً ثم تعدّى حكمه إلى الغير. وعلى هذا الأصل هو أن ما يلزمه أولاً يتعدى إلى غيره تبعاً.
And all types of authority (wilayat) are cut off by slavery, because it is a legal incapacity. And only the aman (safe conduct) of the permitted slave (al-ma'dhun) is valid because the aman, i.e., the slave by permission, goes out of the categories of authority since he has become a partner in the spoils. So it becomes binding on him and then extends to others, like his testimony on the hilal of Ramadan. And upon this principle it is valid. 'Legal incapacity': connected to his saying such as dhimma, permissibility, and authority. And when the author explained dhimma and permissibility, he now begins with authority. So the slave has no authority over others. Authority is the execution of one's statement over others whether they like it or not. That is because slavery is a legal incapacity, rendering the slave incapable of transactions regarding himself. So when the slave has no authority over himself, he has none over others, because a person's authority is first established over himself and then extends to others. Thus the slave has no authority of judiciary, testimony, marriage, and other transitive authorities. 'The aman of the permitted slave is valid' etc.: a refutation of what might be objected against his statement 'and all types of authority are cut off by slavery', namely that on this basis the aman of the permitted slave for the warring disbeliever in jihad would not be valid, because it is an action concerning others by nullifying their rights over the property and lives of disbelievers and their enslavement, and acting over others is authority. The reasoning for the refutation is that the aman of the permitted slave is not from the category of authority. Rather, his aman is valid because by virtue of the master's permission he has become a partner of the fighters in spoils, i.e., the radhkh, meaning he is a responsible human who deserves radhkh, but the master takes his place in what he owns and deserves. So if the permitted slave gives aman during fighting against disbelievers, he has first destroyed his right to the spoils (i.e., radhkh) and then his aman necessarily extends to others. Unlike the restricted slave (mahjur), whose aman is not valid because he does not initially deserve radhkh due to lack of the master's permission. Permission only attaches to him after he returns safely and gainfully by implication, and that is not considered. And al-Tirmidhi said: It has been narrated from 'Umar ibn al-Khattab that he permitted the aman of a slave. And it is narrated from the Prophet that he said: 'The covenant of the Muslims is one; the lowest of them can give binding aman.' [Tirmidhi no. 1079] The meaning of this according to the learned is that whoever among the Muslims gives aman, it is valid on behalf of all of them. I say: This indicates the permission of the slave's aman whether he is permitted (ma'dhun) or not, provided he is a believer, and his aman is valid. This is what Muhammad and al-Shafi'i held. And Abu Hanifa restricted it to the permitted slave. So upon this, what is meant by the slave in the hadith is the permitted slave, for the reason passed. 'Like his testimony' i.e., this aman is like the slave's testimony on the hilal of Ramadan, which is valid and is not from authority, but rather because the slave makes fasting binding on himself first, and then his ruling extends to others. And upon this principle is that what becomes binding on him first extends to others as a consequence.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage addresses the effect of slavery on legal authority (wilaya). The general rule is that slavery cuts off all types of authority because it constitutes a legal incapacity (ajz hukmi). A slave cannot have authority over others because he lacks authority over himself. However, an exception is made for the aman (safe conduct) given by a permitted slave (ma'dhun) during jihad. The passage explains that this aman is not considered an act of authority but rather a consequence of the slave's partnership in the spoils through his radhkh. By granting aman, he first forfeits his own right to spoils, and then that ruling necessarily extends to others. This is analogous to the slave's testimony on the sighting of the Ramadan hilal: he makes fasting obligatory on himself first, and then it applies to others. The passage then presents a dispute: Imam Muhammad and al-Shafi'i hold that any slave (even if not specifically permitted) can give valid aman, based on a hadith from 'Umar and the prophetic saying 'the covenant of the Muslims is one.' Abu Hanifa restricts it to the permitted slave because the unpermitted slave does not have a right to radhkh. The commentary sides with Abu Hanifa's view, interpreting the hadith as referring to the permitted slave. This is a classic Hanafi usul position that limits general texts by specific conditions.

Key Terms
ولاية (wilaya): Legal authority to execute one's will over others.
أمان (aman): Safe conduct granted to enemy combatants, protecting their life and property.
عجز حكمي (ajz hukmi): Legal incapacity, a status that prevents the exercise of rights and duties.
رضخ (radhkh): A token portion of spoils given to a slave who participates in jihad with permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Abu Hanifa restrict the validity of a slave's aman to the permitted slave (ma'dhun)?
A) Because only the permitted slave has full authority like a free man.
B) Because the permitted slave has a right to radhkh, so his aman affects his own right first.
C) Because the unpermitted slave is not a Muslim.
D) Because the hadith specifically mentions only permitted slaves.

Key Takeaway
Slavery cuts off all authority, but the aman of a permitted slave is valid because it first binds himself through his right to spoils, and then extends to others.

Slave's Confession: Hudud, Qisas, and Theft
Explains validity and effects of slave's confession in criminal cases with intra-Hanafi dispute on extant theft.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rulings on a slave's confession in criminal matters and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding extant stolen property when the master denies.

Core Idea
A slave's confession binds him first and harms the master only derivatively; restriction level affects property return.

This passage examines the validity and consequences of a slave's confession in hudud, qisas, and theft. Although a slave has limited capacity, his confession is accepted in matters that primarily harm him (physical penalties) and only secondarily affect his master. The central controversy arises when a restricted slave (mahjur) confesses to stealing property that still exists and the master denies it. The three Hanafi imams offer different views on whether the hand is cut and whether the property is returned immediately or deferred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Confession Types
Note that the passage covers confessions regarding hudud (fixed penalties), qisas (retaliation), and theft, divided into consumed (al-mustahlaka) and extant (al-qā'imah) property. Also note the slave's status: authorized (ma'dhūn) or restricted (mahjūr).
This step sets the scope: all types are covered, but the dispute is specific to restricted slaves and extant property.
2
Understand the Harm Principle
The commentator states that the confession's harm first binds the slave himself (e.g., hand cutting) and only derivatively harms the master. This principle justifies the validity of the confession even for a restricted slave, as the primary effect is on the slave.
This is a key usul point: the rule is built on the gradation of harm (darar).
3
Analyze the Consumed Theft Case
For consumed stolen property (al-mustahlaka), the confession is valid for both authorized and restricted slaves. The consequence is hand cutting but no financial guarantee (damān) because the property is gone.
Unanimous among the three imams; no dispute here.
4
Dissect the Extant Theft Dispute
For extant stolen property, if the slave is authorized, the confession is valid: hand cut and property returned. If the slave is restricted and the master denies, there is a well-known ikhtilāf. Work through each imam's position: Abu Hanifa (hand cut + return), Abu Yusuf (hand cut, no return, guarantee after emancipation), Muhammad (no hand cut, no return, guarantee after emancipation). Understand the reasoning behind each.
The thamarah al-khilāf is immediate vs. deferred property return.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إقراره بالحدود والقصاص، وبالسرقة المستهلكة وبالقائمة صح من المأذون وفي المحجور
وكذا يصح إقراره
اختلاف معروف. وعلى هذا قلنا في جناية العبد خطاً إنه يصير جزاء لجنايته؛ لأن العبد ليس من أهل ضمان ما ليس بمال إلا أن يشاء المولى الفداء، فيصير عائداً إلى الأصل عند أبي حنيفة له، حتى يبطل بالإفلاس،
إقراره: أي العبد مأذوناً كان أو محجوراً. بالحدود إلخ لأن ضرره يلزمه أولاً ثم يتعدى إلى المولى تبعاً. وبالسرقة المستهلكة بأن أقر العبد المأذون أو المحجور: إني سرقت مالاً استهلكته، يصح إقراره، حتى يقطع يده ولا يجب الضمان عليه.
وبالقائمة صح إلخ : أي صح إقرار المأذون بالسرقة القائمة حتى يردّ المال على المسروق منه ويقطع يده. اختلاف معروف: أي في إقرار العبد المحجور بالسرقة القائمة اختلاف إن كذبه المولى، فعند أبي حنيفة حاله يقطع ويرد المال على المسروق منه، وقال أبو يوسف : يُقطع ولا يردّ المال على المسروق منه؛ لأن فيه ضرراً بالمولى، وإقراره في حق الغير غير صحيح، ولكن المرء يؤخذ بإقراره فيضمن مثله بعد الإعتاق، وقال محمد: لايقطع ولا يردّ ولكن يضمن المال بعد الإعتاق؛ لأن إقرار المحجور بكون المال الموجود في يده مال المسروق منه إقرار على المولى؛ لأنه وما في يده مال للمولى، فلايصح إقراره في حق الغير، وإذا لم يصح الإقرار بالسرقة فلا يقطع يده؛ لأن القطع إنما يكون في السرقة، ولكنه عاقل بالغ يؤخذ بإقراره فيوخذ منه مثله بعد الإعتاق. هذا تشريح المقام، فمن شاء أن يطلع على تفصيل المذاهب فيه وعلى أدلتهم فليرجع إلى كتب الفقه.
His confession regarding hadd penalties and qisas, and regarding stolen property that is consumed and that which is extant, is valid from the authorized slave and also from the restricted slave.
And likewise his confession is valid.
A well-known difference of opinion. And upon this we said regarding the accidental homicide by a slave, that he becomes the compensation for his crime, because the slave is not of the people who can guarantee what is not property, unless the master chooses ransom (fidā'), then it returns to the original principle according to Abu Hanifa for him, until it is invalidated by insolvency.
His confession: i.e., the slave, whether authorized or restricted. 'Regarding hadd penalties etc.' because its harm first binds him and then extends to the master derivatively. 'And regarding stolen property that is consumed' — if the authorized or restricted slave confesses: 'I stole property that I consumed,' his confession is valid, so his hand is cut off and no guarantee (damān) is obligatory upon him.
'And regarding that which is extant, it is valid, etc.' — i.e., the confession of the authorized slave regarding extant stolen property is valid, so that the property is returned to the victim and his hand is cut off. 'A well-known difference of opinion' — i.e., regarding the confession of the restricted slave concerning extant stolen property, there is a difference if the master denies it. According to Abu Hanifa, his hand is cut off and the property is returned to the victim. Abu Yusuf said: His hand is cut off but the property is not returned to the victim because it entails harm to the master, and his confession in the right of another is not valid, but the person is held to his confession and will guarantee the like after emancipation. Muhammad said: He is not cut off nor is the property returned, but he will guarantee the like after emancipation because the restricted slave's confession that the property in his hand belongs to the victim is a confession against the master, since he and what is in his hand are the property of the master. So his confession in the right of another is not valid, and if the confession of theft is not valid, his hand is not cut off because cutting is only for theft. However, he is a sane adult and is held to his confession, so the like is taken from him after emancipation. This is the dissection of the case; whoever wishes to examine the detailed madhhabs and their proofs should refer to books of fiqh.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage discusses the validity and effects of a slave's confession (iqrār) in criminal matters. The matn states that a slave's confession regarding hudud (fixed penalties), qisas (retaliation), and theft (both consumed and extant property) is valid for both the authorized slave (ma'dhūn) and the restricted slave (mahjūr). The commentator explains that this is because the harm of the confession first binds the slave himself (e.g., by imposing hadd or qisas) and only derivatively harms the master. For example, if a slave confesses to stealing and consuming the property, his hand is cut off, and no financial guarantee (damān) is required because the property is already consumed. For extant stolen property (al-qā'imah), if the slave is authorized, his confession is valid, and the property is returned to the victim and his hand is cut off. However, if the slave is restricted (mahjūr) and the master denies the confession, there is a well-known disagreement: Abu Hanifa holds that the hand is cut off and property is returned, because the confession brings harm to the slave first (the hand) and then the property is returned as a necessary consequence. Abu Yusuf says cut the hand but do not return the property because that would harm the master directly; the slave will be liable for the equivalent after emancipation. Muhammad says neither cut nor return; the slave will be liable for the equivalent after emancipation, because the restricted slave's confession regarding property in his possession is effectively a confession against the master's ownership, which is invalid; however, the slave is still bound by his own statement to pay compensation later. The passage then transitions to the case of accidental homicide, which will be covered in the next lesson.

Key Terms
الإقرار (al-iqrār): Confession — a person's admission against himself, which can establish liability for hadd, qisas, or financial obligations.
السرقة المستهلكة (al-sariqa al-mustahlaka): Consumed stolen property — stolen goods that have been used up or destroyed, so no return is possible.
السرقة القائمة (al-sariqa al-qā'imah): Extant stolen property — stolen goods that still exist and can be returned to the victim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling when a restricted slave (mahjur) confesses to stealing extant property and the master denies the confession?
A) The slave's hand is not cut off, and the property is not returned.
B) The slave's hand is cut off, but the property is not returned.
C) The slave's hand is cut off, and the property is returned.
D) The slave is not punished but must pay after emancipation.

Key Takeaway
A slave's confession is valid in criminal matters because the primary harm falls on the slave, but the immediate return of extant property is disputed among the Hanafi imams when the master denies.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
10 min
Ignorance from Gharib al-Sunnah Is Not an Excuse
States the rule that certain ignorance is not an excuse with examples and refutations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when an act of ijtihad based on a solitary hadith is considered impermissible ignorance in Hanafi usul and justify the rejection using textual proofs.

Core Idea
Ignorance from following a solitary hadith that contradicts the Quran or well-known sunna is no excuse—established texts override weak evidence.

This lesson introduces a fundamental barrier to the validity of ijtihad: when a scholar relies on a solitary hadith (gharib min al-sunnah) that contradicts explicit Quranic verses or widely transmitted sunna, their ignorance of the stronger proof does not excuse the error. The author presents four classic Hanafi-Shafi'i disagreements where the opposing school yields to weaker evidence. By working through these cases, you will see how the Hanafi school consistently prioritizes clear texts over solitary reports or flawed analogy.

Guided Path
1
State the Principle
Read the opening sentence: acting upon a gharib hadith contrary to the Book or mashhur sunna is rejected and invalid, and ignorance is not an excuse. Identify the two types of evidence that override the solitary hadith: the Quran and well-known sunna.
Gharib here means a hadith that is unfamiliar or not widely transmitted, especially one that contradicts stronger evidence.
2
Examine the First Example – Sale of Ummahat al-Awlad
Follow the Hanafi refutation of Dawud al-Isfahani's view. Note the opponent's proof (hadith of Jabir) and the Hanafi response: the hadith is abrogated (mansukh) by later prohibition during Umar's caliphate. The well-known sunna prohibits sale, supported by hadiths from Ibn Abbas and Umar.
Abrogation is a key factor: the solitary report contradicts established practice and was abrogated.
3
Examine the Second Example – Intentionally Omitting Tasmiya
Analyze the Shafi'i position: they permit intentional omission based on a hadith ('tasmia in the heart of a believer') and qiyas on forgetfulness. The Hanafi refutation cites Quran 6:121 as explicit prohibition and invalidates the analogy because forgetfulness is not analogous to intention.
The Quranic text is qat'i and overrides the solitary hadith.
4
Examine the Third and Fourth Examples – Qasama and One Witness with Oath
For qasama, the Hanafi school restricts it to blood money only, rejecting qisas, while Shafi'i (old view) allowed qisas under lawth. For one witness and oath, Shafi'i accepts it as a substitute for a second witness, citing a hadith. The Hanafi refutation relies on Quran 2:282 and the hadith 'al-bayyinatu 'ala al-mudda'i' to require two witnesses.
These examples show the pattern: each opposing view relies on a solitary hadith or qiyas that contradicts a clear text.
5
Synthesize the Rule
Conclude that any ijtihad based on gharib hadith or qiyas that contradicts the Book or mashhur sunna constitutes jahl (ignorance) that is not a valid excuse. Even if the scholar claims ijtihad, the error is not excused because the correct evidence was accessible.
This principle limits the scope of legitimate ikhtilaf in Hanafi usul.

أو عمل بالغريب من السنة على خلاف الكتاب أو السنة المشهورة مردود باطل ليس بعذر أصلاً، مثل الفتوى ببيع أمهات الأولاد، وحل متروك التسمية عامداً، والقصاص بالقسامة والقضاء بشاهد ويمين. بيعها: مردود أي كما جهل الباغي وصاحب الهوى مردود لا يصلح عذراً كذلك جهل هؤلاء مردود. ببيع أمهات الأولاد: ذهب داود الأصفهاني ومن تابعه إلى جواز بيع أم الولد متمسكاً بما روى أبو داؤد عن جابر الله قال: بعنا أمهات الأولاد على عهد رسول الله وأبي بكر. [ابو داود رقم: ٣٩٥٤] وبأن أم الولد مملوكة باليقين وارتفاع المملوكية بالولادة مشكوك. ونحن نقول: هذا مخالف للسنة المشهورة، وهي أن لا يجوز كما روي عن ابن عباس عن النبي قال: 'إذا ولدت أمة الرجل منه فهي معتقة عن دبر منه أو بعده'. رواه الدارمی [رقم ٢٥٧٧] وعن عمر بن الخطاب قال أيما وليدة ولدت من سيدها فإنه لا يبيعها ولايهبها ولا يورثها، وهو يستمتع منها، فإذا مات فهي حرّة. رواه مالك في موطأه [رقم: ١٤٦٦] فالآثار الدالة على منع بيعها قد اشتهرت وتلقاها القرن الثاني بالقبول، وأما حديث جابر فمنسوخ، فإنه قال في آخر الحديث: فلما كان عمر نهانا عنه فانتهينا. رواه أبو داود، وهذا صريح في أنه لم يبلغ خبر النسخ إلى أكثر الناس، فلما جاء زمن عمر وكثر تعامل الناس فيه فنبههم عمر على النسخ فانتهروا عنه، فهذا مخالف للسنة المشهورة والإجماع. وحلّ متروك: عطف على قوله بيع أمهات الأولاد، وقد ذهب الشافعي إلى حلّ متروك التسمية عامداً متمسكا بقوله عليه: 'تسمية الله تعالى في قلب كل امرء مؤمن'، وقياساً على متروك التسمية ناسياً. ونحن نقول: هذا مخالف للكتاب وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تَأْكُلُوا مِمَّا لَمْ يُذْكَرِ اسْمُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ وَإِنَّهُ لفسق﴾ (الأنعام: ١٢١)، والقياس على الناسي غير صحيح. والقصاص بالقسامة: فإذا وجد الرجل مقتولاً في محلة ولا يدرى قاتله حلف خمسون رجلاً من أهل المحلة، فإن حلفوا فعلى أهل المحلة الدية وحبس الآبي حتى يحلف، ولا يجب القصاص بحال، هذا عندنا، وقال الشافعي: إذا كان هناك لوث استحلف الأولياء خمسين يميناً ويقضى لهم بالدية على المدعى عليه، سواء عمدا كانت الدعوى أو خطأ، وهذا قوله الجديد. وفي القديم: إذا حلفوا أنهم قتلوه عمداً فلهم القصاص، وبه قال مالك وأحمد، وإن نكل الأولياء عن اليمين استحلف أهل المحلة، فإذا حلفوا برثوا، وإن نكلوا حكم عليهم بالدية، هذا تحرير المذهبين، وأما أدلتهم فمذكورة في المطوّلات وكل واحد يجهل الآخر فيما خالفه، ويقول: إنه مخالفة للسنة. بشاهد ويمين: فالشافعي يجوز القضاء بشاهد ويمين مكان الشاهد الآخر إذا لم يكن له شاهد آخر، عملاً بما روي أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قضى بذلك. رواه مسلم [رقم: ٤٤٧٢] ونحن نقول: هذا مخالف للكتاب، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿ذَلِكُمْ أَقْسَطُ عِنْدَ اللَّهِ وَأَقْوَمُ لِلشَّهَادَةِ وَأَدْنَى أَلَّا تَرْتَابُوا﴾ (البقرة: ٢٨٢)، أو للحديث المشهور وهو قوله عليه: 'البينة على المدعى عليه'، [الترمذي رقم: ١٣٤١] ففي تلك المسائل ونظائرها إن اعتمد المخالف على القياس فهو عمل منه بالاجتهاد بخلاف الكتاب والسنة وإن اعتمد على الخبر فهو عمل منه بالغريب من السنة على خلاف الكتاب والسنة المشهورة، وكل ذلك جهل لا يصلح عذراً، كذا في 'غاية التحقيق'.
Or acting upon a solitary hadith contrary to the Book or the well-known sunna is rejected, invalid, and not an excuse at all, such as the fatwa permitting the sale of ummahat al-awlad, permitting intentionally omitting the tasmiya, [imposing] qisas by qasama, and judgment by one witness and oath. Its sale: rejected, meaning just as the ignorance of the transgressor and the one following desire is rejected and not a valid excuse, similarly the ignorance of these people is rejected. Regarding the sale of ummahat al-awlad: Dawud al-Isfahani and his followers went to the permissibility of selling a mother of children, holding onto what Abu Dawud narrated from Jabir, may Allah be pleased with him: 'We sold ummahat al-awlad during the time of Allah's Messenger and Abu Bakr.' [Abu Dawud no. 3954] And because the umm walad is certainly owned, and the removal of ownership by childbirth is doubtful. But we say: This contradicts the well-known sunna, which is that it is not permissible, as narrated from Ibn Abbas from the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'When a man's slave-girl gives birth to a child from him, she is emancipated upon his death, from before or after.' Narrated by al-Darimi [no. 2577] And from Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him: 'Any slave-girl who gives birth to a child from her master, he may not sell her, give her, or bequeath her, and he may enjoy her, and when he dies she is free.' Narrated by Malik in his Muwatta [no. 1466]. Thus the traditions indicating prohibition of her sale have become well-known and the second generation accepted them; as for the hadith of Jabir, it is abrogated, for he said at the end of the hadith: 'When Umar came, he forbade us from it, so we stopped.' Narrated by Abu Dawud, and this clearly shows that the news of abrogation did not reach most people. When the time of Umar came and people increased in dealing with it, Umar informed them of the abrogation, so they ceased. This contradicts the well-known sunna and consensus. And 'solving what is omitted': connected to his saying 'sale of ummahat al-awlad'; al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, went to the permissibility of intentionally omitting the tasmiya, holding onto his saying, peace be upon him: 'The tasmiya of Allah is in the heart of every believer,' and by analogy to one who omits it forgetfully. But we say: This contradicts the Book, which is His saying: 'And do not eat of that upon which the name of Allah has not been mentioned, and indeed it is grave disobedience' (al-An'am 121), and analogy to the one who forgets is invalid. And qisas by qasama: when a man is found killed in a locality and his killer is unknown, fifty men from the locality swear; if they swear, then the locality pays the blood money and the one who refuses is imprisoned until he swears, and qisas is never obligatory. This is our view. Al-Shafi'i said: If there is suspicious circumstance (lawth), the heirs swear fifty oaths and judgment is given for blood money against the defendant, whether the claim is intentional or accidental. This is his new opinion. In his old opinion: if they swear that he killed him intentionally, they get qisas; Malik and Ahmad also said this. If the heirs refuse the oath, the locality is made to swear; if they swear, they are free; if they refuse, judgment is given against them for blood money. This is the explanation of the two schools. As for their proofs, they are mentioned in lengthy works. Each one is ignorant of the other in what he opposes, and says it is opposition to the sunna. Regarding one witness and an oath: al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, permits judgment by one witness and an oath in place of the second witness when he does not have another witness, acting upon what is narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, judged by that. Muslim narrated it [no. 4472]. But we say: This contradicts the Book, which is His saying: 'That is more just in the sight of Allah and more upright for testimony and more likely that you will not doubt' (al-Baqarah 282), or the well-known hadith which is his saying, peace be upon him: 'The burden of proof is on the claimant' [Tirmidhi no. 1341]. In these issues and their parallels, if the opponent relied on qiyas, then that is acting by ijtihad contrary to the Book and sunna; if he relied on a khabar, then that is acting by a solitary hadith contrary to the Book and the well-known sunna. All of that is ignorance that is not a valid excuse, as in Ghayat al-Tahqiq.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from a Hanafi usul work stating an important principle: certain forms of ignorance are not acceptable excuses in Islamic law. Specifically, ignorance that arises from acting upon a solitary or unfamiliar hadith (gharib min al-sunnah) that contradicts the Quran or the well-known sunna is rejected. The author provides four concrete examples where some scholars (like Dawud al-Isfahani, al-Shafi'i, and others) have held opinions based on weak evidence, and the Hanafi response refutes them. These examples are: (1) selling ummahat al-awlad (slave mothers of children), (2) intentionally omitting the basmalah before slaughtering, (3) applying qisas (retaliation) based on qasama (collective oaths), and (4) judging by a single witness and an oath. In each case, the Hanafi school argues that the opposing view relies either on a solitary hadith that is abrogated or contradicted by stronger evidence, or on qiyas that is invalid because it contradicts a clear text. The passage emphasizes that such ignorance, even if based on some form of ijtihad, is not a valid excuse because the correct ruling is established by explicit Quranic verses or well-known hadith. The authority of this ruling is from later Hanafi scholarship (fatawa/mutakhkhirin period), as indicated by the reference to 'Ghayat al-Tahqiq'.

Key Terms
غريب من السنة (gharib min al-sunnah): A solitary or unfamiliar hadith that contradicts the Quran or well-known sunna; acting upon it is invalid.
جهل لا يصلح عذراً (jahl la yasluhu 'udhran): Ignorance that does not serve as a valid legal excuse, especially when it stems from neglecting established proofs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this lesson, why does the Hanafi school reject the permissibility of selling ummahat al-awlad?
A) Because the hadith of Jabir is weak in chain
B) Because the practice was prohibited by Umar and the hadith is abrogated
C) Because it is qiyas on something else
D) Because there is consensus against it

Key Takeaway
Ignorance based on acting upon a solitary hadith (gharib min al-sunnah) that contradicts the Quran or well-known sunna is not a valid excuse in Hanafi usul.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Hazl in the Amount of Price: The Named Price Prevails
Expansion of a matn on hazl in sale, focusing on the amount of price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on hazl in the amount of price and explain why Abu Hanifa and his two companions differ, applying the usul principle of preferring the expressed term.

Core Idea
When parties jest about the price amount, Abu Hanifa enforces the named price; Sahibayn enforce the secret agreement.

This passage from Muntakhab al-Husami addresses a subtle intra-school dispute over the effect of hazl (jest) on the consideration in sale. The first section deals with hazl in the amount of the price. The parties openly state a higher price (e.g., 2000 dirhams) but secretly agree on a lower one (1000). The commentator expands on the matn by detailing four scenarios of subsequent intention and records the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the two companions. This lesson takes you through the analytical steps to understand the ruling and the underlying usul reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sections and the first section's four scenarios
The passage divides into two sections: hazl in the amount of the price (first) and hazl in the type (second). The first section has four scenarios: (1) parties disregard the jest, (2) they are silent, (3) they disagree on building or disregarding, (4) they build on the jest.
These scenarios are derived from the commentarial expansion.
2
Locate the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn in the first section
Abu Hanifa holds the named price (2000) valid in all four scenarios. The two companions distinguish: if the parties were serious about the contract but jested about the amount, the secret agreement (1000) is enforced. Their difference stems from whether the jest can be isolated or overrides the expression.
The Sahibayn argue that the jest about the amount does not conflict with contract validity, so the hidden agreement can be given effect.
3
Analyze the usul principle behind each position
Abu Hanifa relies on the principle that the contract is formed by expressed terms (zahir al-'aqd). The jest about the amount is void, so only the named price remains. The Sahibayn give priority to the actual intention (batin) when it can be implemented without violating the contract's core. This is a classic usul tension between zahir and batin.
The commentator further explains that if the parties later disagree, the named price is safer.
4
Compare with the analogous ruling in marriage (qiyas)
The passage draws an analogy: in a marriage contract where the dowry is stated in jest but the real dowry is different, both sides agree the actual dowry is valid when they build on the jest. This shows consistency across contract types.
This qiyas supports the Sahibayn's view on amount, but the overall dispute remains.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما فرغ المصنف عن بحث الهزل بأصل العقد شرع في الهزل بقدر العوض وبجنس العوض فقال: ولو تواضعا على البيع بألفي درهم أو على البيع بمائة دينار على أن يكون الثمن ألف درهم فالهزل باطل، والتسمية صحيحة في الفصلين عند أبي حنيفة له، وقال صاحباه يصح البيع بألف درهم في الفصل الأول، وبمائة دينار في الفصل الثاني؛ لإمكان العمل بالمواضعة في الثمن مع الجد في أصل العقد في الفصل الأول دون الثاني، وإنا نقول بأنهما جدا في أصل العقد الفصل من جانب أبي حنيفة والعمل بالمواضعة في البدل يجعله شرطا فاسدا في البيع أي قبول بعض البدل أحا بمائة دينار : هذا نظير للهزل في جنس العوض والتسمية صحيحة إلخ المراد بالفصل الأول هو الهزل في قدر الثمن بأن سميا في العقد ألفين عند الناس والثمن في الحقيقة ألف ففي هذه الصورة لايخلو الحال عن الأقسام الأربعة، فإن أعرضا أي اتفقا على الإعراض عن المواضعة بالهزل صح العقد، وكان الثمن هو المسمّى وهو الألفان بالاتفاق، أو سكتا أي اتفقا على أنه لم يحضرهما شيء من البناء والإعراض، أو اختلفا في الإعراض والبناء، فالمعتبر عند أبي حنيفة رحله التسمية وهو ألفان، وقال صاحباه يعتبر المواضعة فكان الثمن هو الألف، و بطل الألف الذي هزلا به، أو بنيا أي اتفقا على البناء على المواضعة بالهزل فالمعتبر عنده المسمّى وهو وعندهما الألف، وهذا ما بينه المصنف في المتن والمراد بالفصل الثاني هو الهزل في جنس الثمن بأن تواضعا على التسمية عند الناس بمائة دينار، ويكون الثمن في الواقع ألف درهم صح البيع وكان الثمن هو المسمّى، وهو مائة دينار بالاتفاق على كل من الأحوال الأربعة. الفان في الفصل الثاني والحاصل إنما الاختلاف في الفصل الأول دون الثاني، فعندهما في الفصل الأول يجب الألف. في أصل العقد إلخ يعني لا تعارض بين المواضعة بالجد في أصل العقد وبين المواضعة بالهزل في مقدار الثمن، فيمكن الجمع بينهما بأن يجعل العقد منعقداً في الألف الذي في ضمن الألفين ويبطل الألف الآخر الذي هزلا به؛ لأنه غير مطالب لاتفاقهما على الهزل وكل شرط لا مطالب له من العباد لا يفسد به العقد، ولا حاجة إلى اعتبار هذا الألف في تصحيح العقد، فكان ذكره والسكوت العقد، فكان ذكره والسكوت عنه سواء كما في النكاح، فإنه لو تزوجها على ألفين هازلاً والمهر في الواقع ألف ثم اتفقا على البناء على الهزل السابق فالمهر ألف اتفاقاً. الثاني: إذ لا يمكن الجمع بين المواضعة بالهزل في جنس الثمن وبين المواضعة بالجد في أصل العقد؛ لأن المواضعة بالجد في أصل العقد يقتضي صحة العقد، والمواضعة بالهزل في جنس الثمن يقتضي خلو العقد عن الثمن في البيع؛ لأن المذكور هو مائة دينار، وهي ليست مثمناً لأجل الهزل، والألف المقصود لم تذكر، والثمن ما يذكر في العقد، وخلوّ العقد عن الثمن يفسد البيع، فلا بد أن يترك أحدهما، فتركنا المواضعة بالهزل في جنس الثمن، وأخذنا بالجد في العقد ترجيحاً لجانب المصحح بأنهما جداً إلخ: حيث قصدا بيعاً جائزاً.
When the author finished discussing hazl in the contract itself, he began discussing hazl in the amount of consideration and in the type of consideration, saying: 'And if they mutually agree [in jest] on a sale for two thousand dirhams, or on a sale for one hundred dinars with the condition that the price be one thousand dirhams, then the hazl is invalid, and the naming is valid in both sections according to Abu Hanifa. His two companions said: the sale is valid for one thousand dirhams in the first section, and for one hundred dinars in the second section; because it is possible to give effect to the agreed-upon price with seriousness in the contract in the first section but not the second. And we say: they were serious in the contract, the section from Abu Hanifa's side, and giving effect to the agreed-upon price in the substitute makes it a corrupt condition in the sale, i.e., accepting part of the substitute?' 'One hundred dinars': this is analogous to hazl in the type of consideration, and the naming is valid etc. The intended first section is hazl in the amount of the price, such that they named two thousand in the contract publicly while the real price is one thousand. In this case, the situation does not avoid the four categories: if they turn away (i.e., agree to disregard the jest agreement), the contract is valid and the price is the named one, which is two thousand by agreement; or if they are silent (i.e., agree that neither building upon nor disregarding occurred), or they disagree on building or disregarding, then according to Abu Hanifa the named price (two thousand) is considered, but his two companions consider the agreed-upon price (one thousand), and the thousand they jested about is void; or if they build upon the jest agreement, then according to Abu Hanifa the named price is considered, while his two companions consider it as one thousand. This is what the author clarified in the text. The intended second section is hazl in the type of price, such that they agree to name one hundred dinars in public while the real price is one thousand dirhams. The sale is valid and the price is the named one hundred dinars by agreement in all four states. 'Two thousand' in the second section? The upshot is that the difference is only in the first section, not the second. According to the two companions, in the first section the price must be one thousand. 'In the contract etc.' meaning there is no conflict between the serious intention in the contract and the jest about the amount of price; it is possible to combine them by making the contract valid for the thousand within the two thousand and voiding the other thousand they jested about, because it is not claimable due to their agreement on jest, and any condition that is not claimable by people does not corrupt the contract. There is no need to consider this thousand for the validity of the contract; mentioning it or remaining silent about it are the same, as in marriage: if one marries with a dowry of two thousand in jest while the actual dowry is one thousand, and then they agree to build on the previous jest, the dowry is one thousand by agreement. The second: because it is impossible to combine the jest about the type of price with the serious intention in the contract, because the serious intention in the contract necessitates the validity of the contract, while the jest about the type of price necessitates the contract being devoid of a price in the sale, because what is mentioned is one hundred dinars, which is not a price due to the jest, and the intended one thousand is not mentioned. The price is what is mentioned in the contract, and the contract being devoid of a price invalidates the sale. So one of them must be abandoned. We abandon the jest about the type of price and adopt the seriousness in the contract, preferring the side that validates, because they intended a valid sale.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on a matn discussing the effect of hazl (jest) on the consideration in a sale contract. The commentator explains the author's classification into two sections: hazl in the amount of the price (first faṣl) and hazl in the type of the price (second faṣl). For each section, there are four scenarios based on the parties' subsequent intentions: (1) they agree to disregard the jest, (2) they are silent (no intention either way), (3) they disagree on whether they were building on the jest or disregarding, (4) they agree to build on the jest. The commentator records a legal dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that the named price in the contract is the valid price in all scenarios of the first section, because the contract is based on what is expressed. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) distinguish: if the parties were serious in the contract but jested about the amount, the actual agreed-upon price (the lesser amount) prevails, treating the extra amount as a void condition. In the second section (jest about the type), there is agreement that the named price (e.g., 100 dinars) is valid, because the parties cannot simultaneously be serious about the contract and jest about the type of price—the jest would leave the contract without a price, which is impossible. So they must choose seriousness. This illustrates the usul principle that when two intentions conflict, one is prioritized to uphold the contract. The passage also makes a qiyas with marriage contract regarding the dowry, showing consistency across different types of contracts.

Key Terms
المواضعة (al-muwāḍa‘a): Mutual agreement to feign or pretend, especially regarding the price in a contract with jest.
البناء على الهزل (al-binā’ ‘alā al-hazl): To build upon the previous jest, i.e., to treat the jest as binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first section (hazl in amount of price), when the parties agree to build on the previous jest, what is the price according to the two companions?
A) The named price (2000 dirhams)
B) The actual agreed price (1000 dirhams)
C) The contract is invalid
D) Half of the named price

Key Takeaway
In hazl over the amount, the named price is enforceable according to Abu Hanifa, but the secret agreement prevails according to Sahibayn, with the difference turning on whether the jest can be isolated from the contract's substance.

Hazl in the Type of Price: Unanimity and Analogical Reasoning
Expansion on the second section of hazl in sale, focusing on unanimity and analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why all Hanafi scholars agree that the named price prevails when the jest is about the type of price, and identify the analogical reasoning (qiyas) with the marriage contract.

Core Idea
When parties jest about the type of price, the contract would be void if the jest were honored, so seriousness is assumed and the named price stands.

The second section of the passage deals with hazl in the type of price, e.g., stating the price as 100 dinars but secretly agreeing it should be 1000 dirhams. Unlike the first section, here there is no dispute: all scholars hold the named price valid. This lesson explores why the type differs from the amount, and how the commentator strengthens the argument through an analogy with marriage. You will understand the usul principle that when two intentions conflict and one leads to invalidity, the other is adopted to save the contract.

Guided Path
1
Understand the second section: hazl in the type of price
The parties name one type of price (e.g., 100 dinars) but secretly agree on a different type (e.g., 1000 dirhams). The commentator explains that in all four scenarios (disregard, silence, disagreement, building), the named price (100 dinars) is valid by agreement.
This is unlike the first section where there is a dispute.
2
Recognize the reasoning behind unanimity
If the jest were honored, the contract would lack a price because the named price (dinars) is not the intended price, and the intended price (dirhams) is not stated. A contract without a price is invalid. Therefore, to save the contract, the seriousness prevails over the jest. This is a rule of preference (tarjih) to uphold validity.
The principle: 'When two possibilities conflict, the one that validates the act is preferred.'
3
Analyze the qiyas with marriage
The marriage analogy is drawn: if the dowry is stated jestingly but the real dowry differs, and the parties build on the jest, the actual dowry is enforced. This analogy supports the idea that building on jest can give effect to hidden intention. However, in the type scenario, building on the jest is not possible because it would leave the contract without a price, so the named price stands.
The qiyas here is used to contrast the two sections, not to support a dispute.

البناء على الهزل (al-binā’ ‘alā al-hazl): To build upon the previous jest, i.e., to treat the jest as binding.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced

Abu Hanifa's Distinction: Jest in Sale vs. Marriage – A Case Study in Qiyas and Tafriq
Exposition of a usul dispute on hazl in contracts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a void condition (shart fasid) corrupts sale but not marriage to evaluate analogies (qiyas) between contracts and distinguish the correct ruling.

Core Idea
A void condition invalidates a sale but not a marriage; the underlying ʿilla (effective cause) breaks the analogy.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text examines a dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions regarding the effect of jest (hazl) on the consideration in sale vs. marriage. The two companions analogize sale to marriage, arguing that in both contracts the lesser amount should be owed. Abu Hanifa rejects the analogy because sale is corrupted by a void condition, while marriage is not. Understanding this distinction is key to mastering how Hanafi usul uses tafriq (differentiation) to limit qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting stipulations
In both sale and marriage, there is a stipulation by earnestness in the original contract and a stipulation by jest in the amount of consideration. Identify the content of each: earnestness establishes the contract, jest affects the amount.
The jest is about the amount (e.g., saying 2000 when real is 1000).
2
State the Hanafi ruling for each contract
In sale, the earnest stipulation takes precedence, so the named amount (2000) is due. In marriage, both can be combined: marriage valid with lesser dower (1000).
This is Abu Hanifa's position; the companions differ.
3
Analyze the companions' qiyas
The two companions analogize sale to marriage: they argue that in both, the lesser amount should be due because the jest invalidates the higher amount.
They use the same illa: jest about consideration.
4
Examine Abu Hanifa's tafriq (differentiation)
Abu Hanifa points out that sale is corrupted by a void condition (shart fasid), while marriage is not. Therefore, in sale the jest stipulation becomes a void condition that corrupts the contract, making it impossible to combine both stipulations. In marriage, the void condition does not corrupt, so both can be acted upon.
The presence of shart fasid in sale breaks the analogy.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In sale, the buyer must pay the full named price (2000) according to Abu Hanifa, but only the real price (1000) according to the companions. In marriage, all agree the lesser dower (1000) is due.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القياس عوارض مكتسبة فيفسد البيع، فكان العمل بالأصل أولى من العمل بالوصف عند تعارض المواضعتين فيهما، وهذا بخلاف النكاح حيث يجب الأقل بالإجماع؛ لأنّ النكاح لا يفسد بالشرط الفاسد فيفسد البيع وحاصل جواب أبي حنيفة له أن قولكم (وهو إمكان الجمع بين المواضعة بالهزل في مقدار الثمن وبين المواضعة بالجد في أصل العقد غير مسلّم؛ لأنه يمكن الجمع بينهما كما لا يمكن في الفصل الثاني؛ إذ المواضعة بالهزل في مقدار البدل، وهو الثمن تجعل اشتراط قبول الألف الزائد الذي خرج عن الثمنية بالمواضعة شرطاً فاسداً للعقد، لا بمنزلة اشتراط قبول ما ليس من مقتضيات العقد، وهو شرط فاسد يفسد البيع، مع أن فيه للطالب وإن لم يطلبه؛ لأن عدم الطلب بواسطة الرضاء لا يفيد الصحة كالرضى بالربا، وفيه اندفاع لما قـالا بــه والمواضعة بالجد في أصل العقد يقتضي صحة العقد، فإذا لم يمكن الجمع بينهما اخترنا المواضعة بالجد في أصل العقد؛ لأنها مواضعة في الأصل، وهو العقد وتركنا المواضعة في قدر الثمن؛ إذ هي مواضعة في الوصف. فيهما: أي في الأصل والوصف، وقد عرفت تعارض المواضعتين فيهما. لما فرغ من القسم الأول من الإنشاء وهو ما يحتمل النقض شرع في القسم الثاني، وهو ما لا يحتمل النقض، وهو على ثلاثة أقسام: القسم الأول: ما كان المال فيه تبعا كالنكاح القسم الثاني ما لا مال فيه أصلاً كالطلاق الخالي عن المال، القسم الثالث: ما كان المال فيه مقصوداً مثل الخلج والعتق على مال. ثم القسم الأول على ثلاثة أوجه الأول الهزل بأصله والثاني الهزل بقدر البدل الثالث الهزل في جنس البدل، ثم كل وجه من تلك الوجوه على أربعة أوجه بأن اتفقا على البناء أو على الإعراض أو سكتا، أو اختلفا فقال: وهذا إلخ. يجب الأقل: أي أقل المهر فيما هزلا به هذا شروع في القسم الأول، وهو ما كان المال فيه تبعاً كالنكاح، فإن المقصود الأصلي من الجانبين الحلّ الذي يحصل به التوالد والتناسل، والمال فيه لإظهار خطر المحل لا مقصوداً، فيكون تبعاً، وهذا نظير للهزل في قدر البدل وهو المهر، وصورةً بأن قال لها أو لوليّها: المهر في الواقع ألف، والتسمية عند الناس بألفين، ووافقه المرأة أو وليها على ذلك فالنكاح صحيح مطلقاً في الأحوال كلها، لكن في وجوب المسمّى أو ما تواضعا عليه تفصيل، وهو أنه إن اتفقا على الإعراض عن المواضعة بالهزل فاللازم هو المهر المسمّى، وهو ألفان بالاتفاق لبطلان المواضعة بالإعراض عنها ، أو اتفقا على البناء على المواضعة بالهزل فالمعتبر هو المواضعة بالهزل، ويكون المهر هو الألف الذي تواضعا عليه بالاتفاق أيضاً، وهذا ما بينه المصنف في المتـ وهذا بخلاف البيع حيث يجب الألفان عند أبي حنيفة به، وعندهما الألف قياساً على النكاح. ووجه الفرق هو أن قبول العقد في الألف الذي هزلا به شرط فاسد كما مرّ في البيع، فلا يمكن اعتباره في البيع؛ إذ هو يفسد بالشرط الفاسد بخلاف النكاح. فأمكن العمل بالمواضعتين ولو ذكرا في النكاح الدنانير وغرضهما الدراهم يجب مهر المثل؛ لأن النكاح يصحّ بغير تسمية بخلاف البيع، ولو هزلا بأصل النكاح فالهزل باطل والعقد لازم. قوله عليها ثلاث جدهن جدّ، وهزلهن......] وكذلك الطلاق والعتاق والعفو عن القصاص واليمين والنذر؛ صحيح العمل بالمواضعتين إحداهما المواضعة بالجد بأصل النكاح والأخرى المواضعة بالهزل في مقدار المهر، والعمل على تلك المواضعة لاينافي العمل بالمواضعة بالجد بأصل النكاح؛ لأن مقتضى الأولى تصحيح النكاح، وتلك المواضة لاتنافي صحة النكاح؛ إذ غايتها أنها شرط فاسد يخل بالمهر ، والنكاح لا يفسد بالشرط الفاسد بل لا يضره عدم تسمية المهـــر، فأمكن الجمع بينهما، فالعمل بالأولى أفاد صحة النكاح، والعمل بالأخرى أفاد وجود أقل المهر وهو الألف الألف، فاندفع قياس الصاحبين، حيث قاسا البيع على النكاح؛ لأن البيع يفسد بالشرط الفاسد، فلا يمكن الجمع بين المواضعتين فيـــه كما مر تقريره منا، أو سكتا أي اتفقا على أنه لم يحضرهما شيءٌ أو اختلفا في البناء والإعراض فالمعتبر و المسمّى فيجب ألفان كما في البيع، وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف ولو ذكرا أي الزوج والزوجة أو وليها. وغرضهما الدراهم إلخ هذا نظير للهزل في جنس البدل، وهذا أيضا على أربعة أوجه والنكاح في كل الوجوه بالاتفاق، وإنما الكلام في وجوب المسمّى الوجه الأول: هو إن اتفقا على الإعراض عن الهزل فالمهر هــو المسمّى، وهو مائة دينار لبطلان المواضعة بالإعراض والوجه الثاني: هو إن اتفقا على البناء فمهر المثل بالاتفاق؛ لأن المسمّى لا يصلح مهراً لقصدهما الهزل به والمال لا يثبت بالهزل، وكذا الدراهم التي تواضعا عليها؛ لأنهما لم يذكراها في العقد، وبدون الذكر فيه لايصير مهراً، فصار كأنه تزوجها على غير المهر ولكن لايفسد النكاح بخلاف البيع: حيث لا يصح بغير تسمية الثمن، فإذا خلا البيع عن الثمن فسد فلا يمكن الجمع بين المواضعتين في الهزل بجنس الثمن، وفي الجد بأصل البيع كما مرّ تقريره، وهذا الوجه بينه المصنف في الكتاب والوجه الثالث هو السكوت، والوجه الرابع هو التخالف، ففي هذين الوجهين يجب مهر المثل اتفاقاً في رواية عن أبي حنيفة له، وهو رواية محمـــد لله لأن المهر تابع، فيجب العمل بالهزل كيلا يصير المهر مقصوداً بالصحة؛ إذ لا حاجة لانعقاد النكاح إلى صحته. لما فرغ عن الهزل في قدر البدل وجنسه شرع في الهزل بأصله. بأصل النكاح بأن يقول لها: إني أنكحت بحضور الخلق، وليس بيننا نكاح أو قال لوليها: إني أنكح فلانة وليس بيننا نكاح. والعقد لازم سواء اتفقا على البناء أو الإعراض، أو عدم حضور شيء منهما، أو اختلفا فيه. ولما فرغ عن القسم الأول شرع في القسم الثاني، وهو ما لا مال فيه أصلاً فقال: وكذلك أي مثل النكاح في بطلان الهزل بأصله ولزوم العقد.
Chapter of Qiyas: Acquired impediments. Then the sale becomes corrupt, so acting upon the original is better than acting upon the description when the two stipulations conflict in them. This is contrary to marriage where the lesser is obligatory by consensus because marriage is not corrupted by a void condition. Then the sale becomes corrupt. And the summary of Abu Hanifa's response to them is that your saying (the possibility of combining the stipulation by jest in the amount of the price and the stipulation by earnestness in the original contract is not conceded; because it is possible to combine them as it is not possible in the second section. For the stipulation by jest in the amount of the substitute, which is the price, makes the condition of accepting the extra thousand that left the price-ness by stipulation a void condition for the contract, not like the condition of accepting what is not from the requirements of the contract, and it is a void condition that corrupts the sale, and it contains for the seeker even if he did not seek it; because the lack of seeking by means of consent does not benefit validity like consent to usury. And in it there is a repulsion of what they said. And the stipulation by earnestness in the original contract necessitates validity of the contract. So when it is not possible to combine them, we choose the stipulation by earnestness in the original contract because it is a stipulation in the original, which is the contract, and we leave the stipulation in the amount of the price because it is a stipulation in the description. In them: i.e., in the original and the description, and you have known the conflict of the two stipulations in them. When he finished from the first section of construction, which is what is susceptible to annulment, he began the second section, which is what is not susceptible to annulment, and it is of three divisions: the first division: that in which property is subordinate like marriage; the second division: that in which there is no property at all like divorce free from property; the third division: that in which property is intended like khul' and manumission for a consideration. Then the first division has three aspects: the first is jest in its original, the second is jest in the amount of the substitute, the third is jest in the genus of the substitute. Then each aspect of those aspects has four aspects: that they agree on building upon it, or on disregarding, or they remain silent, or they disagree. So he said: etc. The lesser: i.e., the lesser of the dower in what they jested about. This is a commencement of the first division, which is that in which property is subordinate like marriage, for the original intent from both sides is the licit enjoyment that results in procreation, and property in it is to show the significance of the subject, not intended, so it becomes subordinate. And this is analogous to jest in the amount of the substitute, which is the dower. Its form is that he said to her or her guardian: the dower in reality is one thousand, and the naming among people is two thousand, and the woman or her guardian agreed with him on that. Then the marriage is absolutely valid in all states, but regarding the obligation of the named or what they stipulated upon, there is detail: if they agreed on disregarding the stipulation by jest, then what is necessary is the named dower, which is two thousand by consensus, due to the annulment of the stipulation by disregarding it; or they agreed on building upon the stipulation by jest, then the basis is the stipulation by jest, and the dower is the one thousand that they stipulated upon by consensus as well. And this is what the author explained in the text. And this is contrary to the sale where the two thousand are obligatory according to Abu Hanifa by it, and according to the two companions the thousand by analogy to marriage. And the point of difference is that accepting the contract regarding the thousand that they jested about is a void condition as previously in sale, so it cannot be considered in sale because it is corrupted by the void condition, unlike marriage. So it is possible to act upon both stipulations. And if they mention in marriage dinars and their intent is dirhams, the dower of the like is obligatory because marriage is valid without specification, contrary to sale. And if they jest about the original of marriage, then the jest is invalid and the contract is binding. His statement: 'upon her three, their earnestness is earnest, and their jest is ...' Likewise divorce, manumission, pardon from qisas, oath, and vow; the jest is valid? Actually, 'valid'? Acting upon both stipulations, one of which is the stipulation by earnestness in the original of marriage and the other is the stipulation by jest in the amount of the dower. Acting upon that stipulation does not contradict acting upon the stipulation by earnestness in the original of marriage, because the requirement of the first is the validation of marriage, and that stipulation does not contradict the validity of marriage since its limit is that it is a void condition that affects the dower, and marriage is not corrupted by a void condition, nor is it harmed by the lack of naming the dower. So it is possible to combine them. So acting upon the first benefits the validity of marriage, and acting upon the other benefits the existence of the lesser dower, which is the thousand. So the analogy of the two companions is repelled, where they analogized sale to marriage because sale is corrupted by the void condition, so it is not possible to combine the two stipulations in it as per our previous explanation. Or they remained silent, i.e., they agreed that nothing was present to them, or they disagreed regarding building and disregarding, then the basis is the named dower, so two thousand are obligatory as in sale, and it is a narration from Abu Yusuf. And if they mention, i.e., the husband and wife or her guardian, and their intent is dirhams, etc. This is analogous to jest in the genus of the substitute, and this also has four aspects, and marriage in all the aspects is by consensus, and the discussion is only about the obligation of the named. The first aspect: if they agree on disregarding the jest, then the dower is the named, which is one hundred dinars, due to the annulment of the stipulation by disregarding. The second aspect: if they agree on building, then the dower of the like is by consensus, because the named is not suitable as dower due to their intent to jest with it, and property is not established by jest. Similarly, the dirhams that they stipulated upon because they did not mention them in the contract, and without mentioning them they do not become dower, so it is as if he married her without a dower, but it does not corrupt the marriage, contrary to sale, which is not valid without naming the price. So if the sale is devoid of the price, it is corrupted, and it is not possible to combine the two stipulations in jest concerning the genus of the price and in earnestness concerning the original of the sale, as per our previous explanation. And this aspect the author explained in the book. The third aspect is silence, and the fourth aspect is disagreement. In these two aspects, the dower of the like is obligatory by consensus in one narration from Abu Hanifa, and it is a narration from Muhammad, because the dower is subordinate, so acting upon the jest is obligatory so that the dower does not become intended with validity, since the validity of the marriage is not dependent on its (the dower's) validity. When he finished from jest in the amount of the substitute and its genus, he began jest in its original. Regarding the original of marriage: that he says to her: I have married you in the presence of people, but there is no marriage between us; or he says to her guardian: I marry so-and-so, but there is no marriage between us. And the contract is binding whether they agree on building or disregarding, or nothing is present from them, or they disagree. And when he finished from the first division, he began the second division, which is that in which there is no property at all, and he said: Likewise, i.e., like marriage in the invalidity of jest in its original and the binding nature of the contract.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the Hanafi rulings on jest (hazl) in contracts, specifically comparing sale and marriage. It begins by stating a principle: when there is a conflict between two stipulations (mawda'atan) — one involving jest in the amount of consideration and the other involving earnestness in the original contract — the priority is given to the original over the description. In sale, such a conflict invalidates the contract because the void condition corrupts it, unlike marriage where the lesser amount is due by consensus. The author then summarizes Abu Hanifa's response to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) who analogize sale to marriage. Abu Hanifa argues that combining the two stipulations is not possible in sale because the jest about the price constitutes a void condition that corrupts the contract; in marriage, such a condition does not invalidate the marriage, so the stipulations can be combined, leading to the validity of the marriage with the lesser dower. The text then proceeds to categorize contracts based on the role of property: where property is subordinate (like marriage), where there is no property (like divorce), and where property is intended (like khul' and manumission for a price). For the first category, there are three types of jest: jest in the original (asl), jest in the amount of the substitute (qadr al-badal), and jest in the genus of the substitute (jins al-badal). Each type has four sub-scenarios based on whether the parties agree to build upon the jest, disregard it, remain silent, or disagree. The author provides details for each scenario, always emphasizing that marriage is more tolerant of void conditions than sale. The key distinction is that sale is invalidated by a void condition (shart fasid) and requires a specified price for validity, whereas marriage remains valid even with a void condition regarding the dower, and the dower can be determined by the actual agreement or by default (mahr al-mithl) if the named one is jested. The passage also covers jest in the original of marriage, confirming that the contract is binding regardless of the parties' intent. It concludes by noting that similar rulings apply to divorce, manumission, pardon from qisas, oaths, and vows: the earnest is taken seriously, and jest does not affect validity.

Key Terms
هزل (hazl): Jest or joke in a legal context; statements made without serious intent. In contracts, it may affect the obligation but not the validity of the contract itself.
مواضعة (mawda'a): A stipulation or understanding between parties; can be either earnest or jesting. The text discusses conflicting mawda'at.
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): A condition that is void in Islamic law, typically one that contradicts the nature of the contract or a legal principle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does Abu Hanifa reject the analogy (qiyas) of the two companions that sale should follow the ruling of marriage in cases of jest about the consideration?
A) Because the two companions are not qualified to make qiyas.
B) Because sale is invalidated by a void condition, while marriage is not, making the analogy invalid.
C) Because there is a consensus (ijma) that sale requires the full price.
D) Because the jest in sale is always about the original contract, not the description.

Key Takeaway
The effect of a void condition depends on the contract's tolerance; sale is invalidated, marriage is not, thus the same type of jest yields different results.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
10 min
Effect of Huzl in Khul' Divorce: Hanafi Usul Analysis of Jest and Ikhtilaf
Usul al-fiqh analysis of huzl in khul' with intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that huzl in khul' creates a conditional suspension of divorce, and identify the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Jest (huzl) in khul' does not void the contract but suspends divorce on the woman's choice, like an option condition.

This passage examines the effect of jest (huzl) in a khul' divorce contract within Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The key question is whether huzl nullifies the contract or suspends it pending the woman's serious confirmation. The text presents Abu Hanifa's position that huzl is analogous to an option condition (khiyar al-shart), making divorce conditional on the woman's choice, and contrasts it with the Sahibayn's view that huzl is void ab initio. Understanding this ikhtilaf illuminates how Hanafi jurists use qiyas and the nature of contracts (isqat vs. ithbat) to derive rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and ikhtilaf
State Abu Hanifa's position: huzl suspends divorce on the woman's choice. Then state the Sahibayn's opposing view: huzl invalidates the jest, making the divorce immediate.
The ikhtilaf is limited to three specific scenarios (jest in origin, amount, or type of compensation).
2
Trace the Hanafi analogy to khiyar al-shart
Note that Abu Hanifa analogizes huzl to an option condition (khiyar al-shart). Just as in khiyar al-shart the divorce does not occur until the woman chooses, so too with huzl. This analogy is the key proof (dalil) for his position.
The text cites a narration from Abu Hanifa on khiyar al-shart: 'divorce does not occur, and payment is not obligatory unless she chooses.'
3
Understand the distinction between khul' and sale (isqat vs. ithbat)
Abu Hanifa explains that khiyar al-shart in sale is limited to three days because sale is ithbat (establishing ownership), and the option is against qiyas. Khul', however, is isqat (dropping of rights), so the option is in accordance with qiyas and can be unlimited.
This distinction is crucial for the scope of the option: in khul', the woman's option is not restricted to three days.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf in the three contested scenarios
In scenarios where the parties jest in the origin, amount, or type of compensation, and they agree on the jest, Abu Hanifa says divorce depends on her choice; the Sahibayn say divorce and payment are immediate.
In the other nine scenarios (e.g., no agreement on jest or different facts), there is consensus.

خيار الشرط في الخلع
yؤثر فيه الهزل إذا اتفقا على البناء،
الجهتين، فلا منافاة وكلامنا في التابع باعتبار الثبوت والمال في النكاح ليس بتابع في الثبوت؛ إذ هو يثبت بدون الذكر أيضا، وإنما هو تابع بالنظر إلى العاقدين، لأن قصدهما الحل دون المال، فإذا لم يكن تابعاً في الثبوت فيؤثر فيه الهزل كما في سائر الأموال، وأما المال في الخلع فهو تابع في الثبوت حيث لا يثبت بدون الشرط فلايؤثر فيه الهزل، فافترقا بكل حال سواء هزلا بأصله أو بقدر البدل أو بجنسه فيتوقف ثبوت الطلاق على اختيار المرأة. من جانبها أن رجلا لو قال لامرأته: أنت طالق ثلاثا على ألف درهم على أنك بالخيار إلى ثلاثة أيام. تشاء المرأة: أي إن اختارت المرأة الطلاق في ثلاثة أيام، أو لم ترد حتى مضت المدة. فكذلك هنا: أي كما أن وقوع الطلاق ووجوب المال يتوقف على اختيار المرأة في خيار الشرط كذلك في صورة الهزل؛ لأن الهزل بمنزلة خيار الشرط، ولما كان يتوهم أن الخيار من جانبها في الخلع إنما صح عند أبي حنيفة يالله لكونه في معنى البيع؛ لأن ثبوته في جانبها باعتبار معنى المعاوضة، وخيار الشرط في البيع مقدّر بالثلاث، فكان ينبغي أن يكون في الخلع كذلك دفعه بقوله: لكنه إلخ بالثلاث لأن الشرط في الخلع على وفاق القياس؛ لأنه من قبيل الإسقاط، فإنه طلاق، فيجوز تعليقه بالشرط مطلقاً من غير تقييده بمدة، فعلى هذا فلها الخيار فوق الثلاث، بخلاف البيع فإن خيار الشرط فيه على خلاف القياس؛ لأنه من قبيل الإثبات، فاقتصر على مورد النص وهو ثلاثة أيام في نظائره: أي كما يثبت الحكم والاختلاف في الهزل بالخلع، كذلك في نظائره من الهزل بالطلاق على مال والصلح عن دم العمد، يعني الكل سواء في حكم، والاختلاف. إذا اتفقا على البناء على المواضعة سواء كان الهزل بأصل العقد أو بقدر البدل أو بجنسه. اعلم أن ثمرة الخلاف إنما يترتب في تلك الصور الثلاث، وهي ما لو هزلا بأصل العقد أو بقدر البدل أو بجنسه، واتفقا على البناء على المواضعة فعندهما كما يبطل الهزل ويلزم المال في جميع الوجوه كذلك يبطل الهزل ويلزم المال في تلك الصور أيضا لا يتوقف على اختيارها بناءً على أصلهما، وعند أبي حنيفة الله يتوقف وقوع الطلاق في هذه الصور الثلاث على اختيار المرأة الطلاق بالمسمّى على طريق الجد وإسقاط الهزل بناءً على أصله. وأما الصور التسع الباقية، فلا خلاف فيها، =
Chapter of Qiyas. 315. Acquired impediments. According to Abu Hanifa (may Allah be pleased with him), the divorce is suspended on her choice in every case; because it is like the option condition. It has been narrated from Abu Hanifa regarding his ruling on option condition from her side: that the divorce does not occur, and the payment is not obligatory unless the woman chooses, then divorce occurs and payment is obligatory. Likewise here, but it is not limited to three days, and likewise in its analogues. Then it is necessary to act upon the convention (muwada'a) in that which is affected by huzl if they agree upon building (al-bina'). From both sides, no contradiction. Our discussion is on the dependent (tabi') in terms of establishment (thubut), and the wealth (mal) in marriage is not dependent in establishment; for it is established without mention as well. Rather it is dependent with respect to the two contractors, because their intention is [marital] permissibility without wealth. So if it is not dependent in establishment, then huzl affects it as in other wealth. As for the wealth in khul', it is dependent in establishment where it is not established without the condition, so huzl does not affect it. Thus they differ in every case, whether they jest in its origin, in the amount of the compensation, or in its type, then the establishment of divorce is suspended on the woman's choice. From her side, if a man says to his wife: 'You are divorced thrice for one thousand dirhams on the condition that you have the option for three days.' The woman chooses: i.e., if she chooses divorce within three days, or she does not intend until the period passes. Likewise here: just as the occurrence of divorce and obligation of wealth depend on the woman's choice in the option condition, so too in the case of huzl; because huzl is like the option condition. And since it might be thought that the option from her side in khul' is only valid according to Abu Hanifa because it is in the meaning of sale – for its establishment on her side considers the meaning of exchange, and the option condition in sale is limited to three days, so it should be so in khul' – he refutes it by saying: 'But it is not limited to three days' because the condition in khul' is in accordance with qiyas; for it is of the type of isqat (dropping of rights), as it is divorce, so it is permissible to suspend it on a condition absolutely without restriction to a period. Thus she has the option beyond three days, unlike sale where the option condition is contrary to qiyas; for it is of the type of ithbat (establishment of rights), so it is confined to the text's limit of three days. In its analogues: just as the ruling and disagreement are established in huzl in khul', likewise in its analogues of huzl in divorce for money and sulh (settlement) for intentional bloodshed, meaning all are equal in ruling and disagreement. If they agree upon building on the convention (muwada'a), whether the huzl is in the origin of the contract, in the amount of the compensation, or in its type. Know that the fruit of the disagreement only arises in those three scenarios: if they jest in the origin of the contract, or in the amount of the compensation, or in its type, and they agree upon building on the convention. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), just as huzl is invalidated and payment is obligatory in all aspects, so too huzl is invalidated and payment is obligatory in those scenarios as well, not depending on her choice based on their principle. According to Abu Hanifa, the occurrence of divorce in these three scenarios depends on the woman's choice of divorce with the named amount in a serious manner and dropping huzl, based on his principle. As for the remaining nine scenarios, there is no disagreement in them =
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh work (possibly a commentary on al-Hidayah) presents a detailed ruling on the effect of jest (huzl) in a khul' divorce contract. The author begins by stating Abu Hanifa's position: when a khul' is done in jest, the divorce is suspended on the woman's subsequent choice, similar to an option condition (khiyar al-shart). The text explains that just as in khiyar al-shart from the woman's side the divorce does not occur unless she chooses, so too in huzl. However, unlike khiyar al-shart in sale which is limited to three days, in khul' the option is not so limited because khul' is a form of isqat (dropping of rights) and can be suspended on any condition. The passage then discusses the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). According to the companions, huzl is void ab initio, and the contract is serious; thus divorce and payment are immediate without depending on the woman's choice. Abu Hanifa treats huzl like an implied option, so the woman must choose for the divorce to take effect. The text enumerates three specific scenarios where huzl occurs in the origin, amount, or type of compensation, and where the parties agree to build on the jest. In these, the disagreement applies. In the other nine scenarios (e.g., where they do not agree or the jest is not in these aspects), there is consensus that the divorce occurs and payment is obligatory. The passage also clarifies that if the parties disagree whether there was jest or not, the contract is presumed serious, and the word of the one claiming seriousness is accepted. This ruling illustrates how Hanafi jurists balance textual principles (qiyas, istihsan) and practical considerations in contractual matters.

Key Terms
الهزل (al-huzl): Jest or playful intent that accompanies a legal act, potentially affecting its validity.
الخلع (al-khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation (usually monetary) paid by her to the husband.
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): A stipulation in a contract giving one party an option to confirm or rescind within a specified period.
الإسقاط (al-isqat): The dropping or surrender of a right, as in khul' where the wife drops her marital right in exchange for compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is the woman's option in khul' not limited to three days?
A) Because the Prophet (PBUH) allowed unlimited options in all contracts.
B) Because khul' is a form of isqat, which is in accordance with qiyas, so the condition can be absolute.
C) Because the couple can agree to any term, including an unlimited option.
D) Because khul' is a sale, and options in sale are unlimited.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, huzl in khul' does not void the contract but rather suspends the divorce on the woman's choice, analogized to an option condition, with the crucial distinction that khul' is isqat, making the option unlimited.
